It is home to some of the most copied holes in the world, most notably the 15th, "Redan" which has been replicated on nearly every continent. Unlike many modern courses, North Berwick is famous for its quirks—including stone walls that must be lofted over and ancient, deep-seated bunkers.

The club has hosted every major amateur event and served as a Final Qualifying venue for the Open Championship for decades. Notable members have included legends of the game and icons of the Scottish establishment. The 13th hole, "Pit" requires an approach over a historic stone wall to a green nestled on the other side. North Berwick is a "fun" links in the truest sense; it is a creative, unpredictable, and spiritually uplifting journey along the Firth of Forth. To play here is to experience the very soul of Scottish golf architecture.

North Inch
The North Inch Golf Course in Perth is a site of immense historical significance, with records of golf being played on this common land as far back as 1512. It is one of the oldest places in the world where the game has been enjoyed. The current layout was designed by the legendary Old Tom Morris, providing a classic parkland-links hybrid experience right in the center of Perth. Because it is built on a flood plain of the River Tay, the turf is remarkably springy and fast-draining.

As a municipal course, the North Inch has been a training ground for generations of Perthshire golfers. It is an open, walking-friendly course that offers views of the historic Scone Palace across the river. While it is a public facility, it is maintained to a high standard and has hosted numerous regional amateur championships. The 18th hole, playing back toward the city's historic spires, is a classic finish. North Inch represents the "people's game"—historic, accessible, and deeply rooted in the origins of the sport.

Oatridge and Binny
Oatridge and Binny Golf Club, located near Broxburn, is a unique and high-quality parkland course that serves as a teaching facility for the Scottish Agricultural College. Opened in the late 1990s, the 9-hole course (played twice for an 18-hole round) was designed by Graeme Webster. It is characterized by its rolling terrain, clever water hazards, and its commitment to ecological diversity. The course is famously well-manicured, as it serves as a "living classroom" for greenkeeping students.

The club is known for its relaxed and welcoming atmosphere, making it a favorite for beginners and those looking for a stress-free round. While it lacks the ancient history of other Lothian clubs, it offers a modern, scientifically-managed playing surface that is often superior to many private tracks. The signature hole requires a precise shot over a large pond to a well-guarded green. Oatridge and Binny is a testament to the future of the game—sustainable, accessible, and professionally maintained—offering a high-value and educational round of golf.

Old Meldrum
Old Meldrum Golf Club is a historic Aberdeenshire parkland course with roots dating back to 1885. The course sits on a high ridge overlooking the "Garioch" countryside, providing expansive views of the peak of Bennachie. The layout is a varied and engaging mix of holes, featuring significant elevation changes and mature woodland. It is a tactical course where the prevailing wind is a major factor, often requiring a creative, low-ball flight.

The club is a focal point of the local community and is known for its competitive amateur teams. While it hasn't hosted the professional majors, it is a regular venue for Aberdeenshire County events and is highly regarded for its consistent conditioning. The signature 13th hole, "The Binn" offers a dramatic tee shot and views that are among the best in the county. Old Meldrum is a traditional, friendly club that provides an authentic "North East" parkland experience, where the quality of the greens and the warmth of the clubhouse are the primary attractions.

Old Ranfurly
Old Ranfurly Golf Club, located in the village of Bridge of Weir, is a classic Scottish moorland course that has been a staple of Renfrewshire golf since 1898. The course was originally laid out by the 1883 Open Champion Willie Fernie and later refined by the legendary James Braid. It is perched on a high plateau, providing some of the most spectacular panoramic views in the West of Scotland, stretching from the Ben Lomond peaks to the Gleniffer Braes.

The club is renowned for its firm, springy turf and its challenging, fast-running greens. Notable members over the years have included various titans of Glasgow's industrial past, and the club remains a prestigious venue for the Renfrewshire County Championships. The layout is notoriously tricky when the wind blows across the exposed moorland, requiring a creative array of "bump and run" shots. It is a traditional, aristocratic club that maintains an impeccably conditioned course, offering a "pure" golfing experience that feels far removed from the urban bustle of nearby Glasgow.

Orkney
Orkney Golf Club, situated just outside Kirkwall, is a rugged and atmospheric parkland-moorland hybrid that offers a truly unique island experience. Established in 1889, the course is one of the most northerly in the UK. The layout is characterized by its significant elevation changes and its exposure to the fierce Atlantic winds, which act as the course's primary defender. From the higher holes, players are treated to cinematic views of the northern islands and the historic St. Magnus Cathedral.

The club is the heart of the Orcadian golfing community and is known for its incredibly warm and unpretentious welcome. While it lacks a "celebrity" architect, the natural routing is genius, using the undulating landscape to create several blind shots and challenging carries over heather and gorse. The greens are remarkably true despite the harsh climate. Notable for its "Midnight Sun" tournaments held during the summer solstice, Orkney Golf Club offers a raw, elemental connection to the game that every adventurous golfer should experience at least once.

Paisley
Paisley Golf Club, often referred to locally as "Bushes" is a magnificent moorland course located within the Gleniffer Braes Country Park. Founded in 1894, the course was redesigned in the 1950s by Philip Mackenzie Ross, the architect responsible for the post-war restoration of the Ailsa course at Turnberry. The layout is perched high above the town of Paisley, offering views that, on a clear day, extend all the way to the southern Highlands and the Cumbrae Isles.

The club has a strong competitive pedigree and has hosted the Scottish Youths' Championship and numerous PGA Scotland regional events. It is characterized by its narrow fairways, thick heather, and strategic bunkering that punishes the wayward driver. Notable for its lush conditioning and challenging par-threes, Paisley is a "thinking man's" course where local knowledge is key to navigating the rolling terrain. It is a friendly, vibrant club that provides a high-quality, championship-standard test of golf in a stunningly scenic and elevated setting.

Palacerigg
Palacerigg Golf Course is a rugged and rewarding moorland layout located within the Palacerigg Country Park in Cumbernauld. Designed by the three-time Open Champion Henry Cotton and opened in the 1970s, the course was built to provide a high-quality public-sector challenge. Cotton utilized the natural peat and heather of the moorland to create a course that feels wild and isolated. It is a relatively long course that requires both power and precision, especially on the exposed holes where the wind is a major factor.

As a municipal facility, Palacerigg has a reputation for being one of the best-value rounds in the central belt. The layout features several significant water hazards and tight fairways lined with young woodland. While it doesn't host the professional majors, it is a staple of the Lanarkshire amateur circuit and is praised for its year-round playability. The signature holes along the ridge offer spectacular views over the Forth Valley. It is an honest, unpretentious course that represents the "Cotton" philosophy of accessible but rigorous golf, providing a peaceful escape for the region's golfers.

Panmure
Panmure Golf Club is a world-class links located in Carnoustie, often cited as one of the most underrated courses in Scotland. Established in 1845, the current layout at Barry Links was designed with input from Old Tom Morris and James Braid. It is famously the place where Ben Hogan spent two weeks practicing before his legendary 1953 Open victory at Carnoustie. Hogan suggested several changes to the 6th hole, which the club adopted and still carries his name today.

The course is a "hidden" links, with many holes winding through dunes and corridors of Scots pine, giving it a unique character compared to the more exposed local tracks. It has served as a Final Qualifying venue for the Open Championship and is a regular host for the Scottish Amateur Championship. The greens are notoriously firm and fast, and the bunkering is among the most strategic in the country. Panmure is a refined, private club that offers a pure and historic links experience, where the ghost of Hogan seems to linger on every fairway.

Peebles
Peebles Golf Club is a spectacular parkland-moorland hybrid situated on the slopes of the Southern Uplands. Established in 1892, the course was significantly redesigned by Harry Colt, one of the giants of golf architecture. The layout is characterized by its dramatic elevation changes and panoramic views over the Tweed Valley. It is a tactical course where the driver is often best left in the bag in favor of accuracy, as the fairways are lined with mature trees and punishing gorse.

The club is a focal point of the local Borders community and has a history of producing elite amateur talent, including former Scottish champions. Notable for its impeccably fast greens and its warm, welcoming clubhouse, Peebles is a regular host for the Borders Golfers' Association championships. The signature 13th hole, "The Neidpath" offers a scenic view that is worth the walk alone. It is a traditional, well-maintained club that provides a refined and physically engaging round of golf, capturing the lush, rolling beauty of the Scottish Borders.

Peterculter
Peterculter Golf Club is a beautiful parkland course located on the banks of the River Dee, just south of Aberdeen. Established in 1989, the course was designed by Graeme Webster to take full advantage of the dramatic riverside setting and the surrounding valley. The layout is a "tale of two halves": the lower holes follow the meandering path of the Dee, while the upper holes climb the hillside, offering expansive views across the Aberdeenshire countryside.

The club is known for its modern, friendly atmosphere and its commitment to high-quality conditioning. While it is a relatively young course, it has quickly established itself as a premier venue for regional PGA Scotland events. The signature par-three 13th, played from a high tee to a green nestled near the riverbank, is one of the most photographed holes in the region. Peterculter is a "resort-style" club in terms of its amenities but remains a community hub at heart. It offers a scenic, varied, and technically demanding round of golf that highlights the natural beauty of the Dee Valley.

Peterhead - Old
Peterhead Old Course is a rugged and authentic links that holds the distinction of being the 18th oldest golf club in the world. Established in 1841 and refined over the years by various hands, the course is situated among some of the most dramatic sand dunes in the North East. It is a pure links experience where the wind off the North Sea is a constant and shifting factor. The layout is characterized by its narrow fairways, deep bunkers, and fast-running turf.

The club has a prestigious history and has hosted various regional amateur championships, known for being a "true" test of links skill. Notable for its isolation and its connection to the local fishing community, Peterhead Old offers a sense of total immersion in the elements. The signature holes through the massive dunes require both power and a delicate touch on the firm greens. It is a traditional, unpretentious club that prides itself on maintaining the integrity of its ancient links land. For those who enjoy the raw, unadulterated side of the game, Peterhead Old is an essential and historic stop.

Peterhead - New
The New Course at Peterhead is the club's delightful 9-hole sibling, offering a quicker but equally scenic links experience. While it is shorter than the Old Course, it shares the same high-quality turf and stunning coastal views. The layout is designed to be more accessible for juniors, beginners, and those looking for a fast "nine" after work, but it still features several tricky holes that require respect.

The New Course is maintained by the same dedicated greenkeeping team as the Old, ensuring that the playing surfaces are of a championship standard. It serves as a vital entry point for the local community into the sport and offers a more relaxed environment for casual play. Despite its name, the course has a mature feel and blends seamlessly into the rugged coastal landscape. It is the perfect example of how a historic club can provide a comprehensive golfing experience, catering to all levels of ability while honoring its links heritage.

Piperdam
Piperdam Golf & Leisure Resort is home to the Newtyle course, a premier 18-hole parkland layout situated near Dundee. Opened in the mid-1990s, the course was designed to be a centerpiece for the surrounding holiday resort. It is a modern "target-style" course characterized by its significant water hazards—including a massive central loch—and its large, undulating greens. The layout is relatively flat but is punctuated by strategic bunkering and mature woodland.

The resort has a high-energy, modern atmosphere and is a favorite for corporate golf days and society outings. While it may not have the ancient history of the nearby links, it offers a professional-standard parkland experience with world-class facilities. Notable for its impeccable conditioning and its "amen corner" around the loch, Piperdam is a regular host for regional PGA Scotland pro-ams. The signature 18th hole, requiring a carry over water to a green overlooked by the lodge balcony, provides a theatrical finish. It is a high-value destination for those seeking a modern and visually stunning round of golf in the heart of Angus.

Pitlochry
Pitlochry Golf Club is frequently described as the "Switzerland of Scotland." Established in 1908 and refined by the legendary Willie Fernie, this 18-hole course offers a unique "inland links" experience perched on the edge of the Highlands. It is famous for its steep elevation changes, particularly the climb on the opening holes which is rewarded with breathtaking views over the Tummel Valley. The course is characterized by springy, moorland turf and fairways lined with heather and silver birch.


The club has a vibrant, modern atmosphere and has hosted the Highland Open since 1921, drawing competitors from across the globe. Notable for its friendly "pro-shop" culture, the course is often cited as one of the best-conditioned in Perthshire. The signature 4th hole, "The Brae" requires a heroic drive up a steep incline, while the closing stretch offers a series of thrilling downhill holes where the ball seems to travel forever in the crisp Highland air. It is a scenic masterpiece that proves you don't need a coastline to have a world-class golfing adventure.

Pitreavie
Pitreavie Golf Club in Dunfermline is a site of immense architectural interest, having been designed by the legendary Dr. Alister MacKenzie in 1922. MacKenzie, who later designed Augusta National and Cypress Point, brought his revolutionary "multi-tier" green design to the Fife countryside. The course is a polished parkland layout that features many of MacKenzie's signature trademarks, including strategic bunkering that uses shadows to deceive the eye and greens that require masterclass-level reading.


The club has a strong competitive history and frequently hosts the Fife County Championships. It is a regular stop for serious students of golf architecture who come to see the early work of the "Calamity Jane" designer. Notable for its impeccably fast greens and its lush, mature tree-line, Pitreavie offers a refined and intellectual round of golf. The 18th hole provides a dramatic finish in front of the traditional clubhouse, requiring a precise approach to one of the most complex greens on the course. It is a high-quality, historic track that offers a taste of "Master's" style strategy in the heart of Scotland.

Paul Lawrie Golf Centre
The Paul Lawrie Golf Centre, located just outside Aberdeen, is a state-of-the-art facility founded by the 1999 Open Champion, Paul Lawrie. The 9-hole course at the centre is designed to Lawrie's exacting standards, providing a world-class "short course" experience that emphasizes iron play and short-game precision. Despite its shorter yardage, the course features tour-quality greens and strategic bunkering, making it a favorite practice ground for local professionals and elite amateurs.

The centre is a hub for the Paul Lawrie Foundation, which has been instrumental in developing the next generation of Scottish golfers. It features a world-class driving range and teaching academy, reflecting Lawrie's commitment to the growth of the game. While it is a public-access facility, the conditioning is of a championship standard. For those looking to sharpen their skills or enjoy a quick, high-quality round, the centre provides a modern and professional environment. It is a testament to Lawrie's legacy, offering an accessible gateway to elite-level training and play.

Polkemmet
Polkemmet Golf Course is a delightful 9-hole parkland layout situated within the Polkemmet Country Park in West Lothian. Developed on the site of a former private estate, the course was opened in the 1980s and has matured into a scenic and testing facility. The layout winds through mature woodland and features several significant water hazards, including the River Almond which comes into play on the early holes.

As a municipal facility, Polkemmet is known for its inclusive and friendly atmosphere. While it is a shorter course, it requires a high degree of accuracy off the tee to navigate the narrow, tree-lined corridors. It is a favorite for local families and seniors, offering a tranquil and affordable "stroll in the park" that still provides enough challenge to keep experienced players on their toes. Notable for its excellent drainage and year-round playability, Polkemmet represents the best of community golf—offering a peaceful escape and high-quality turf in a historic estate setting.

Pollok
Pollok Golf Club is one of Glasgow's most prestigious and refined parkland sanctuaries. Established in 1892 and redesigned in the 1920s by Dr. Alister MacKenzie, the course is situated within the magnificent Pollok Country Park. It is a "pure" golf club in the traditional sense, maintaining an atmosphere of quiet elegance and impeccable standards. The layout is characterized by its lush, manicured fairways and greens that are widely considered to be among the finest in the West of Scotland.

The club has a storied history and has hosted many prestigious amateur and professional events, including the Scottish Amateur Championship. Notable members have historically included leaders of Glasgow's merchant and professional classes. The course is beautifully secluded, with the White Cart Water meandering through the property and providing a natural hazard on several holes. Pollok is a sanctuary of traditional values, offering an uncompromising parkland test where the quality of the conditioning is matched only by the warmth of the clubhouse hospitality.

Port Bannatyne
Port Bannatyne Golf Club, located on the Isle of Bute, is a unique and quirky 13-hole course that offers a truly memorable island experience. Founded in 1912, the course is perched on a hillside overlooking the Kyles of Bute and Loch Striven. Because it consists of 13 holes, a "full" round involves playing five of the holes twice, creating a varied and interesting 18-hole loop. The layout is a rugged moorland hybrid, featuring natural hazards like gorse and heather.

The club is known for its incredible panoramic views and its relaxed, "honesty box" atmosphere. While it lacks a famous architect, the course is a masterclass in utilizing the natural landscape to create a fun and engaging challenge. It is a favorite for visitors who enjoy the "undiscovered" side of Scottish golf. Notable for its springy turf and small, tricky greens, Port Bannatyne rewards the creative player over the long hitter. It is a quintessential island club—peaceful, scenic, and deeply traditional—offering a round of golf that feels like a step back in time.

Port Glasgow
Port Glasgow Golf Club is a rugged and rewarding moorland course situated high above the Firth of Clyde. Established in 1895, the course offers some of the most dramatic views in the region, stretching from the Erskine Bridge to the Argyll hills. The layout is characterized by its significant elevation changes and its exposure to the sea breezes, which act as a constant defender of par. It is a tactical course where local knowledge is key to navigating the various blind shots and sloping fairways.

The club is a focal point of the local community and is known for its unpretentious and welcoming membership. While it doesn't host professional tours, it is a stalwart of the Renfrewshire amateur circuit and has produced many fine local champions. The greens are remarkably true and often quite fast in the summer months. Notable for its peaceful, elevated setting, Port Glasgow provides a spirited and challenging round of golf that captures the rugged beauty of the Clyde coastline. It is an honest, traditional club that offers high-value golf with a view that is hard to beat.

Portlethen
Portlethen Golf Club, located just south of Aberdeen, is a modern and highly-regarded parkland course that was founded in 1981. Designed by Donald Steel, one of the most respected modern golf architects, the course was built to provide a championship-standard test for the growing local community. The layout features wide, rolling fairways, strategic water hazards, and large, subtly undulating greens. It is a course that rewards both length and precision, making it a fair but formidable test.


The club has a vibrant and professional atmosphere, frequently hosting regional PGA Scotland events and the Aberdeenshire County Championships. Notable for its impeccable conditioning and its "Tour-standard" practice facilities, Portlethen has quickly become one of the premier inland courses in the North East. The signature 15th hole, a par-three played over water to a well-guarded green, is a highlight of the round. It is a polished, high-gloss club that offers a modern and engaging golfing experience, perfect for those who appreciate contemporary design and world-class maintenance.

Portmahomack
Portmahomack (Tarbat) Golf Club is a beautiful 9-hole links course situated on the shores of the Dornoch Firth. Established in 1909, the course is a traditional, natural links that offers spectacular sea views from every hole. The layout is characterized by its firm, sandy turf, deep bunkers, and gorse-lined fairways. It is a "pure" links experience where the wind off the Moray Firth is a constant and shifting factor, requiring a creative array of low-ball flight shots.

The club is an "honesty box" facility and is maintained with immense pride by the local community. While it lacks a "celebrity" architect, the routing is genius, utilizing the natural dunes and shoreline to create a varied and engaging challenge. It is a favorite for those traveling the North Coast 500 who want to experience an authentic Highland links without the crowds. Notable for its peace and seclusion, Portmahomack offers a raw, elemental connection to the origins of the game. It is a hidden gem that rewards the adventurous golfer with a truly memorable and scenic round.

Portobello
Portobello Golf Course is a charming 9-hole parkland course located in the heart of Edinburgh's seaside suburb. As a municipal facility, it has served as a vital nursery for the game in the capital for over a century. The course is relatively short and flat, making it an ideal venue for beginners, juniors, and seniors. Despite its modest length, the layout features several well-placed trees and small greens that require a steady hand and precise club selection.

The club is known for its relaxed and inclusive atmosphere, providing an accessible gateway for the local community into the sport. While it doesn't boast a famous architect or championship pedigree, it is a beloved local asset that is maintained to a good standard. Its proximity to the city center and the Portobello beach makes it a popular choice for a quick "nine" after work or on the weekend. Portobello represents the "social" side of the game—unpretentious, affordable, and focused on the enjoyment of the sport in a friendly and urban setting.

Portpatrick Dunskey
Portpatrick Dunskey Golf Club is a spectacular cliff-top links-style course located on the rugged coast of Wigtownshire. Established in 1903, the course was refined in the early 20th century by the legendary James Braid, who took full advantage of the dramatic elevation changes. The layout is perched high above the Irish Sea, and on a clear day, the views stretch all the way to the coast of Northern Ireland. It is a scenic masterpiece where the sound of the waves crashing against the cliffs is a constant companion.

The club has a friendly and welcoming atmosphere, frequently hosting regional South of Scotland amateur championships. Notable for its firm, springy turf and its exposure to the "Portpatrick breeze" the course requires a creative array of shots. The signature holes along the cliff edge are among the most photographed in the country, requiring nerve as well as skill to avoid the rocky drops. It is a traditional club that offers a wild, exhilarating, and visually stunning round of golf, making it a "must-play" for anyone touring the South West.

Portpatrick Dinvin Course
The Dinvin Course at Portpatrick is the club's delightful 9-hole sibling, providing a shorter but equally scenic challenge. While it measures significantly less than the main Dunskey course, it is no simple "warm-up." The Dinvin is a par-three course that features small, tricky greens and several significant natural hazards. It is maintained to the same high standards as the main track, offering manicured playing surfaces and the same stunning coastal views.

The course is particularly popular with families, beginners, and those looking to sharpen their short game. It serves as a vital training ground for the club's thriving junior section. Many members use the Dinvin for a quick evening round when time is short, enjoying the peaceful environment and the brisk sea air. It is a perfect example of how a premier club can offer a comprehensive experience for all skill levels, ensuring that the enjoyment of the game remains accessible to everyone in a world-class setting.

Powfoot
Powfoot Golf Club is one of the most respected "hidden" links in Scotland, situated on the shores of the Solway Firth. Founded in 1903, the course was designed by the esteemed James Braid, who created a unique hybrid layout—part links and part parkland. The course begins and ends on traditional links land, while the middle section moves inland to more sheltered, tree-lined fairways. This variety ensures that no two holes at Powfoot feel the same.

The club has a significant tournament history, frequently serving as an Open Championship Regional Qualifying venue and hosting the Scottish Mid-Amateur Championship. Notable for its deep bunkers and fast-running fairways, Powfoot is a "pure" golfer's course that rewards strategic thinking. The views across the Solway toward the Lake District mountains provide a magnificent backdrop. It is a friendly, traditional club that prides itself on its impeccable conditioning, offering a challenging and historic round of golf that punches well above its weight on the national stage.

Prestonfield
Prestonfield Golf Club is a magnificent parkland sanctuary located in the shadow of Arthur's Seat in Edinburgh. Established in 1920, the course was designed by the legendary James Braid, who utilized the naturally rolling terrain of the historic Prestonfield Estate to create a tactical masterpiece. Despite being located just a mile from the city center, the course feels remarkably secluded, with its fairways lined by mature trees and a diverse range of local wildlife.

The club has a prestigious history and has produced many fine amateur players, including former Scottish internationals. Notable for its impeccably fast greens and its challenging par-threes, Prestonfield is a regular host for the Lothians County Championships. The signature view of the "Lion's Head" on Arthur's Seat from the fairway is one of the most iconic sights in Scottish golf. It is a traditional and welcoming club that offers a refined, historic, and physically engaging round, representing the very best of urban parkland design.

Prestwick
Prestwick Golf Club is a hallowed site and the birthplace of The Open Championship, having hosted the very first tournament in 1860. Originally designed by Old Tom Morris, who also served as the club's first keeper of the green, the course is a raw and uncompromising links. It is famous for its eccentricities, including massive dunes, blind shots, and the "Alps" hole—the oldest and most famous blind approach in the world. Prestwick hosted The Open 24 times before the tournament grew too large for the site.

The club remains one of the most traditional and exclusive in the world, yet it offers a warm welcome to visitors looking to walk in the footsteps of the giants of the game. Notable members have historically included the pioneers of modern golf. To play Prestwick is to experience a time capsule of 19th-century links architecture; it is creative, unpredictable, and spiritually moving. Every hole tells a story, from the "Cardinal" bunker to the "Sea Heugh." It is a mandatory pilgrimage for any serious student of the game's history.

Prestwick St Cuthbert
Prestwick St Cuthbert is a premier parkland course that offers a distinct contrast to the famous links neighbors in the town. Established in 1899, the current layout was designed in the 1960s by the respected architect P.M. Ross. The course is characterized by its lush, manicured fairways and its over 1,000 mature trees, creating a parkland oasis in the heart of the "Ayrshire Golf Coast." It is a relatively flat course, making it an easy and enjoyable walk for all ages.

The club has a vibrant and competitive membership, frequently hosting the Ayrshire Strokeplay Championship and regional PGA Scotland events. Notable for its impeccably true greens and strategic bunkering, St Cuthbert is a "fair" test that rewards accuracy and a sharp short game. The traditional clubhouse is known for its excellent hospitality and views over the 18th green. It is a friendly, professional club that provides a high-quality, polished parkland experience, making it a favorite for those looking for a break from the punishing coastal gorse.

Prestwick St Nicholas
Prestwick St Nicholas is a historic and scenic links course located just south of the famous Open venue. Founded in 1851, the club is the 26th oldest in the world, and Old Tom Morris himself was a founding member and a frequent competitor on these fairways. The course is a traditional "out and back" links that hugs the shoreline of the Firth of Clyde, offering stunning views across to the Isle of Arran and the Ailsa Craig.

The layout is characterized by its firm turf, deep bunkers, and the "Quarry" holes that provide a unique and challenging middle section. Notable for its fast greens and its exposure to the sea breezes, St Nicholas is a regular host for the Scottish Ladies' Championship and national senior events. It is a refined and welcoming club that maintains a strong sense of its 19th-century heritage. For those seeking an authentic links experience with deep historical ties to the founders of the professional game, St Nicholas is an essential and rewarding stop.

Pumpherston
Pumpherston Golf Club in West Lothian is a modern parkland success story. Originally a 9-hole course, it was extended to 18 holes in 2002 with a design that emphasizes ecological sustainability and "target" golf. The course is built on reclaimed land and features several significant water hazards and large, undulating greens. It has quickly built a reputation for its year-round conditioning and its commitment to providing a championship-standard test for the local community.

The club is a hub for the West Lothian amateur circuit and is known for its friendly, forward-thinking atmosphere. While it lacks the ancient history of its neighbors, Pumpherston offers a polished and technically demanding round that rewards precision over raw power. The signature holes around the central lakes require a steady nerve and careful club selection. It is a popular venue for society outings and corporate days, offering a modern, professional, and visually stunning golfing experience in the heart of the central belt.

Ralston
Ralston Golf Club, located on the border of Glasgow and Paisley, is a prestigious parkland masterpiece designed by the legendary James Braid. Established in 1913, the course is a model of Braid's strategic design, featuring his signature bunkering and greens that require a sharp eye. The layout is characterized by its lush, mature tree-line and its impeccably manicured fairways, offering a sense of total seclusion despite its proximity to the city.

The club has a proud history and has produced many fine amateur players who have represented Renfrewshire at the highest levels. Notable for its fast, sloping greens and its challenging par-fours, Ralston is a regular host for regional county championships. The clubhouse is a traditional sanctuary that reflects the club's long-standing status as one of the premier inland venues in the West of Scotland. It is a refined, "gentleman's" club that prioritizes the quality of its turf and the traditions of the game, offering an uncompromising parkland test.

Ranfurly Castle
Ranfurly Castle Golf Club, located in the village of Bridge of Weir, is a premier moorland course that dates back to 1889. The current layout was designed by James Braid and is widely considered one of the finest moorland tracks in the country. Perched on a high ridge, the course offers panoramic views stretching to the mountains of the Southern Highlands. The layout is a hybrid of moorland and heathland, featuring natural hazards like heather, gorse, and rocky outcrops.


The club has a significant tournament pedigree, having hosted the Scottish Girls' Championship and various PGA Scotland events. Notable members have included legends of the local industry, and the club remains one of the most prestigious in Renfrewshire. The greens are famously fast and true, while Braid's strategic routing ensures a varied and engaging challenge. The ruins of the 15th-century Ranfurly Castle overlook the course, providing a dramatic historical backdrop. It is a traditional, high-quality club that offers a "pure" and scenic golfing experience in a stunningly elevated setting.

Ratho Park
Ratho Park Golf Club is a stunning parkland sanctuary located on the outskirts of Edinburgh. Established in 1928, the course was designed by the legendary James Braid and is uniquely situated within the confines of an ancient estate wall. This stone boundary creates an atmosphere of total seclusion, shielding the golfer from the outside world. The layout is characterized by its magnificent mature trees—including massive oaks and beeches—that frame the fairways and require precise shot-shaping.


The club has a prestigious reputation and is a regular host for the Lothians County Championships. Notable for its impeccable conditioning and its remarkably flat terrain, it is an easy walk but a difficult "score" as Braid's strategic bunkering and small, fast greens demand respect. The Union Canal runs alongside several holes, adding to the tranquil environment. It is a traditional, refined club that prides itself on maintaining the highest standards of etiquette and turf quality, offering a polished and historic parkland experience that remains one of the most popular in the capital.

Ravelston
Ravelston Golf Club is a hidden gem tucked away in the heart of Edinburgh's affluent West End. Founded in 1912, the course was designed by the esteemed James Braid and is a model of clever routing on a compact site. This 9-hole course (played twice for an 18-hole round) is perched on the slopes of Corstorphine Hill, offering spectacular views over the city toward the Firth of Forth and the mountains of Fife.


The club is known for its privacy and its incredibly friendly, tight-knit membership. Notable for its lush, wooded environment and significant elevation changes, Ravelston provides a tactical challenge where accuracy is far more important than length. The small, well-protected greens are famously tricky to read. While it may not host international championships, it is a cherished part of the Edinburgh golfing scene, offering a peaceful and scenic escape just minutes from the city center. It is the perfect destination for the "thinking" golfer who appreciates historic design and a quiet, aristocratic atmosphere.

Reay
Reay Golf Club holds the distinction of being the most northerly 18-hole links course on the British mainland. Located in Caithness, the course was designed by James Braid and offers a raw, unadulterated links experience on the edge of the Atlantic. The layout is a natural masterpiece, winding through dunes and over springy, sandy turf. On a clear day, the views across the Pentland Firth toward the Orkney Isles are simply breathtaking.

The club is a focal point of the local community and is known for its incredibly warm and unpretentious welcome. Despite its remote location, the course is maintained to a high standard, featuring lightning-fast greens and deep, natural bunkers. Notable for its exposure to the fierce northern winds, Reay requires a masterclass in low-ball flight and "bump and run" shots. It is an "honesty box" facility that represents the very soul of Scottish golf—wild, scenic, and deeply connected to the elements. For those traveling the North Coast 500, a round at Reay is an essential and spiritually uplifting experience.

Renfrew
Renfrew Golf Club is a premier parkland course that has long been considered one of the finest in the West of Scotland. Established in 1894 and moved to its current site in 1970, the course was designed by the respected Commander John D. Harris. It is an 18-hole championship layout characterized by its wide, lush fairways and towering avenues of trees. It has a high tournament pedigree, having served as an Open Championship Regional Qualifying venue for many years.

The club has hosted numerous prestigious events, including the Scottish Amateur Championship and several international matches. Notable for its strategic water hazards and its large, undulating greens, Renfrew is a "fair" but formidable test that rewards the bold player. The signature finishing hole, requiring a carry over water to a green overlooked by the modern clubhouse, is a highlight of the round. It is a professional and welcoming club that offers a polished, high-gloss parkland experience, making it a favorite for competitive golfers and society outings across the central belt.

Roodlea Golf Centre
Roodlea Golf Centre, located in Ayr, is a modern and highly accessible 9-hole parkland course that caters to the local community and visitors to the Ayrshire coast. Opened in the early 2000s, the facility was designed to provide a relaxed and inclusive environment for golfers of all levels. The course is relatively flat and features wide fairways, making it an ideal venue for beginners and juniors, while well-placed bunkers and water hazards provide enough of a challenge for more experienced players.

The centre is particularly renowned for its excellent practice facilities, including a floodlit driving range and a professional coaching academy. While it lacks the ancient history of the nearby Open venues, it has become a vital hub for the "Golf for All" movement in Ayrshire. Notable for its friendly atmosphere and year-round playability, Roodlea offers a high-value and stress-free round of golf. It is the perfect place for a quick "nine" after work or a family outing, representing the modern, welcoming face of the sport in one of Scotland's most famous golfing regions.

Rosehearty
Rosehearty Golf Club is a rugged and charming 9-hole links course located on the Aberdeenshire coast. Established in 1882, it is one of the oldest clubs in the region and offers a traditional, natural links experience. The course is situated right on the water's edge, featuring firm, sandy turf and natural hazards like rocky outcrops and thick gorse. The views across the North Sea are spectacular, especially during the long summer evenings when the light seems to linger on the fairways.

The club is an "honesty box" facility and is maintained with immense pride by a small group of local volunteers. While it doesn't boast a celebrity architect, the routing is a testament to the simplicity of early links design, utilizing the natural contours of the shoreline to create a variety of challenging shots. Notable for its exposure to the North Sea gales, Rosehearty is a place where you must play "with the wind" rather than against it. It is a peaceful, unpretentious, and historic gem that offers a pure and affordable connection to the origins of the game.

Rothes
Rothes Golf Club is a scenic 9-hole parkland course situated in the heart of the Spey Valley, famous for its whisky distilleries. Opened in 1990, the course was designed by Euan McIntosh and is built on a hillside overlooking the village and the River Spey. The layout is characterized by its significant elevation changes and its lush, well-manicured fairways. The surrounding woodland and the backdrop of the Ben Aigan hills provide a tranquil and stunning setting for a round of golf.

The club is a vital part of the local community and is known for its warm, Speyside hospitality. While it is a relatively young course, it has quickly established a reputation for its conditioning and the trueness of its greens. It is a regular favorite for visitors touring the local distilleries who want to balance their whisky tasting with a high-quality round of golf. Notable for its challenging par-threes and its peaceful, secluded atmosphere, Rothes offers a "boutique" golfing experience that captures the natural beauty and the relaxed spirit of the Highlands.

Rothesay
Rothesay Golf Club, located on the Isle of Bute, is a spectacular 18-hole moorland course designed by the legendary James Braid in 1908. Perched on a high plateau, the course offers some of the most panoramic views in the world of golf, stretching across the Firth of Clyde to the peaks of Arran and the mountains of Argyll. It is a rugged, undulating layout that requires both physical stamina and tactical finesse to navigate.

The club has a prestigious history and has produced several notable amateur players. Braid's genius is evident in the way he utilized the natural rocky outcrops and heather as organic hazards. Notable for its firm, springy turf and its challenging, fast-running greens, Rothesay is a "pure" moorland test. The signature holes along the ridge offer views that are worth the ferry trip alone. It is a friendly and traditional island club that offers a wild, exhilarating, and visually stunning round of golf, representing one of Braid's most scenic achievements.

Rouken Glen
Rouken Glen Golf Course is a historic and popular municipal parkland course located within the award-winning Rouken Glen Park in Giffnock, just south of Glasgow. Established in the early 20th century, the course has long been a favorite for city golfers looking for an accessible and well-maintained round. The layout is characterized by its mature trees, rolling fairways, and several significant elevation changes that provide a varied and engaging challenge.


As a municipal facility, Rouken Glen has a reputation for its inclusive and welcoming atmosphere. While it doesn't host professional tours, it has served as a vital training ground for generations of Glasgow golfers. The course is famously scenic, with the park's historic waterfall and woodland providing a beautiful backdrop. Notable for its year-round playability and its friendly clubhouse, Rouken Glen offers high-quality golf at an affordable price. It is a cherished community asset that represents the "people's game" in a setting of exceptional natural beauty.

Routenburn
Routenburn Golf Club is a dramatic and scenic 18-hole moorland course situated on the hills high above Largs. Designed by the legendary James Braid and opened in 1914, the course is famous for its panoramic views over the Firth of Clyde to the islands of Cumbrae and Arran. It is a "mountain-style" layout characterized by steep climbs and thrilling downhill shots, requiring a high level of fitness and a creative approach to the various blind shots.

The club is known for its warm and friendly membership and its unpretentious, traditional clubhouse. Braid's strategic routing ensures that the wind is a constant and shifting factor, making "low-ball" flight essential. Notable for its firm, springy turf and its challenging, sloping greens, Routenburn is a "pure" moorland test that punishes the wayward driver. The signature views from the higher holes are among the most photographed in Ayrshire. It is a high-value and exhilarating club that offers a unique and scenic golfing adventure on the edge of the West Coast.

Rowallan Castle
Rowallan Castle Golf Club is a modern masterpiece set within a historic 600-acre Ayrshire estate. Designed by the eight-time European Number One and Ryder Cup Captain Colin Montgomerie, the course opened in 2009 and quickly gained a reputation for its tour-quality conditioning. The layout winds through mature woodland with the spectacular backdrop of two castles—one 13th-century and one Victorian. Montgomerie utilized the natural undulations to create a "modern classic" featuring cavernous bunkers and large, fast, undulating greens.


The course is a tactical challenge that requires power off the tee but extreme finesse on the greens. Notable for its 19th hole (the "decider"), the club offers a relaxed country club atmosphere. While a relatively new addition to the Scottish circuit, it has hosted numerous PGA Scotland events and is a favorite for high-profile pro-ams. Former Celtic star Murdo MacLeod is a well-known fan of the course. Rowallan provides a polished, luxury experience where the history of the estate meets contemporary championship design, making it a standout in the "Home of Golf."


Roxburghe
The Roxburghe Golf Club, located near Kelso, is arguably the finest inland course in the Scottish Borders. Designed by the internationally renowned architect Dave Thomas and opened by Nick Faldo and Colin Montgomerie in 1997, it is a grand championship parkland layout. The course is set on the Duke of Roxburghe's estate and is characterized by its scale, featuring deep bunkers, sprawling fairways, and the meandering River Teviot.

The club has hosted the Scottish Senior Open and remains a premier venue for professional qualifying events. The signature hole is the par-five 14th, "The Viaduct" where the tee shot is played from an elevated position toward a green framed by the historic Roxburgh Viaduct. It is a "big" course in every sense, rewarding strong driving and bold approach play. With its luxurious clubhouse and estate setting, The Roxburghe offers a world-class, resort-style experience that brings a touch of Gleneagles-style grandeur to the Borders.


Royal Aberdeen - Balgownie
Founded in 1780, Royal Aberdeen is the sixth oldest golf club in the world. The Balgownie Links is a legendary championship venue, originally designed by the Simpson brothers and later refined by James Braid. It is widely regarded as having one of the finest front nines in golf, as the holes weave through massive, ancient dunes that offer total protection from the wind. The back nine moves onto higher ground, providing a more traditional, exposed links challenge with panoramic North Sea views.


The club hosted the 2014 Scottish Open (won by Justin Rose) and the 2011 Walker Cup. Notable members have historically included the elite of Aberdeen's professional classes. The signature 8th hole, "Shelter" is a par-three surrounded by ten bunkers. It is a traditional, prestigious club where the standards of etiquette are as high as the quality of the turf. To play Balgownie is to experience the very essence of traditional Scottish links golf—rugged, historic, and strategically brilliant.

Royal Aberdeen - Silverburn
The Silverburn Course is the shorter, charming sibling to the Balgownie Links. Originally laid out as a recreational loop, it was redesigned by James Braid and offers a delightful mix of links and parkland characteristics. While it measures significantly less than the championship track, it features nine par-threes that test a golfer's iron play and accuracy to the limit. The course is meticulously maintained by the same world-class greenkeeping team as the main links.


Silverburn is a favorite for members seeking a more relaxed round or for those looking to sharpen their short game. It offers the same dramatic coastal views as its elder brother but with a less penal routing. It is often used for junior development and senior tournaments within the club. Despite its "secondary" status, Silverburn is a high-quality track in its own right, providing a peaceful and scenic alternative to the brutal challenge of the Balgownie dunes. It is the perfect "warm-up" for a day at one of the world's most historic clubs.

Royal Dornoch
Royal Dornoch's Championship Course is frequently ranked among the top five golf courses in the world. Golf has been played here since 1616, making it one of the oldest sites in the game. Old Tom Morris extended the course to 18 holes in 1886. It is the spiritual home of the legendary architect Donald Ross, who was born in Dornoch and served as the club's professional before moving to America to design Pinehurst No. 2. Many of Ross's design hallmarks—most notably the inverted-saucer greens—originated here.


The course is a natural masterpiece, winding along the Dornoch Firth with elevated tees and raised greens that require surgical precision. It has hosted the British Amateur and is a site of pilgrimage for legends like Tom Watson, who famously called it the most fun he'd ever had on a golf course. With its iconic yellow gorse and white-sand beaches, Dornoch offers a pure, "timeless" golfing experience. The club recently opened a magnificent new clubhouse in 2025, ensuring that its off-course facilities now match its world-class fairways.


Royal Musselburgh
Royal Musselburgh Golf Club is the fifth oldest club in the world, with roots dating back to 1774. Originally based on the historic Musselburgh Old Links, the club moved to its current site at Prestongrange in 1926. The course was designed by the prolific James Braid and is a quintessential parkland beauty. It is home to the Old Club Cup, the oldest trophy still competitively played for in the world of golf.


The layout is characterized by its lush fairways and mature woodland, offering a sheltered and scenic round. The signature hole is the par-three 14th, known as "The Gully Hole" which requires a carry over a deep, 30-foot ravine to a small green. The clubhouse is a stunning 16th-century mansion house that adds a sense of immense history to the day. While it is located at the start of East Lothian's "Golf Coast" it provides a distinct parkland contrast to the seaside links, maintaining an atmosphere of traditional prestige and community warmth.


Royal Tarlair
Royal Tarlair Golf Club, located in Macduff, is a spectacular cliff-top parkland-links hybrid. Granted its "Royal" status in 1926 by Princess Louise, the course offers some of the most dramatic panoramic views in Aberdeenshire. The layout follows the rugged coastline, with several holes perched precariously above the North Sea. It is a place where the wind is a major factor, and the elevation changes provide a physical and mental test.


The signature hole is the 13th, "Clivet" an enigmatic par-three played from a high tee over a steep valley to a green nestled on a narrow peninsula below. It is widely considered one of the most stunning and nerve-wracking holes in Scotland. The course is adjacent to the village of Pennan, famous as the setting for the film Local Hero. Royal Tarlair is a friendly, unpretentious club that offers a wild and exhilarating round of golf. It is a "hidden gem" in the truest sense, providing world-class views and unique geological challenges for a fraction of the price of the famous links.


Royal Troon - Old
Royal Troon's Old Course is one of the pillars of the Open Championship rotation, having hosted the tournament ten times (most recently in 2024). Designed by Willie Fernie in 1878 and refined by James Braid, it is a traditional "out and back" links. The front nine runs south along the coast, offering scoring opportunities, while the back nine turns into the prevailing wind and is widely considered the toughest finishing stretch in championship golf.

The course is home to two of the most famous holes in the world: the 8th, "The Postage Stamp" the shortest hole in Open golf, and the 11th, "The Railway" bordered by the Glasgow-Ayr train line. Legendary moments here include the 2016 "Duel at Troon" between Henrik Stenson and Phil Mickelson. Notable members have included giants of Scottish industry and sport. To play Troon is to experience a cathedral of the game—a stern, fair, and profoundly historic links that demands the absolute best from every part of your game.


Royal Troon - Craigend
The Craigend Course at Royal Troon is the club's high-quality 9-hole par-three course. While it is often used as a practice facility for members and juniors, it is maintained with the same meticulous care as the Old and Portland courses. Each hole is designed to test short-iron accuracy and putting touch, featuring small, well-bunkered greens that reflect the challenges found on the championship tracks.

The Craigend is a vital part of the club's heritage, providing an accessible gateway for the younger generation to learn the game in a world-class environment. It offers a relaxed and quick round of golf for those who don't have time for the full links experience. Located near the main clubhouse, it provides a peaceful and scenic environment to hone one's skills. While it lacks the international fame of the Old Course, it remains a favorite for members seeking a quiet "nine" in the shadow of the game's greatest amphitheaters.

Royal Troon - Portland
The Portland Course at Royal Troon is a championship-standard links in its own right, originally designed by Willie Fernie and redesigned in 1921 by the legendary Dr. Alister MacKenzie (the architect of Augusta National). Located slightly further inland than the Old Course, it is more sheltered but no less challenging. It features MacKenzie's signature undulating greens and strategic bunkering, requiring a thoughtful approach rather than raw power.


If the Portland were located anywhere else, it would be a world-famous destination. Because it sits next to its "Big Sister" it remains one of the best-value secrets in Ayrshire. It is a favorite for local amateur championships and is often used by members as their "daily" course. Notable for its firm turf and fast greens, the Portland provides a classic links experience without the intimidating length and crowds of the Open venue. It is a "must-play" for any MacKenzie enthusiast and offers a masterclass in strategic golf design.

Saline
Saline Golf Club is a hidden parkland jewel located on the slopes of the Saline Hills in Fife. This 9-hole course is renowned for its elevation and the staggering panoramic views it offers, stretching across the Forth Valley to the Lothians and the Ochil Hills. Established in 1912, the course provides a peaceful, "high-altitude" golfing experience that feels far removed from the busy coastal links of Fife.

The layout is physically demanding due to the hilly terrain, but it rewards the golfer with exhilarating downhill shots and unique architectural quirks. The club is a community-run facility known for its friendly, unpretentious atmosphere. While it doesn't host professional tours, it is a favorite for local society outings. Notable for its lush fairways and small, tricky greens, Saline is a "thinking man's" 9-hole track where accuracy is far more important than power. It is an ideal stop for those looking for a quiet, scenic, and high-value round of golf in the heart of rural Fife.

Sanday
Sanday Golf Club is a rugged and elemental 9-hole links located on the beautiful island of Sanday in the Orkney archipelago. Established in 1897, the course is a throwback to the origins of the game, situated on natural machair land along the shore of Backaskaill Bay. It is a "natural" course in the truest sense, where the fairways are grazed by sheep and the hazards consist of sand dunes, wildflowers, and the unpredictable Atlantic wind.

The club is an "honesty box" facility and serves as the social heart of the island's golfing community. While it lacks a professional designer, the routing follows the natural contours of the coast, providing a raw and authentic links experience. Playing Sanday is as much about the environment as the sport—it is a place of total silence, interrupted only by the sea and the birds. For the adventurous golfer, it offers a rare opportunity to play the game exactly as it was centuries ago, in a setting of haunting northern beauty.

Sandyhills
Sandyhills Golf Club is a premier parkland course located on the eastern edge of Glasgow. Founded in 1905, the course was famously described by golf writer Theodore Moon as "a piece of Old Troon set down four miles from George Square." This 18-hole layout is remarkably well-sheltered from the surrounding city, offering a tranquil and mature environment characterized by its lush fairways and the "Battle Burn" which meanders through the property.

The club has a strong competitive history in the Glasgow and Lanarkshire amateur circuits. Notable for its strategic bunkering and its fast, true greens, Sandyhills is a "fair" test that rewards accurate iron play. The course has matured beautifully over the last century, with thick avenues of trees framing every hole. It is a welcoming, professional club that provides a high-quality "urban oasis" experience, making it one of the most popular and respected inland venues in the West of Scotland.

Sanquhar
Sanquhar Golf Club is a scenic and historic 9-hole parkland-moorland course located in the Nith Valley in Dumfries and Galloway. Established in 1894, the current layout was designed by the legendary Willie Fernie, the 1883 Open Champion. The course is situated on the hills overlooking the town and the ruins of Sanquhar Castle, providing a dramatic and historic backdrop to the round.

The club is known for its warm, South of Scotland hospitality and its impeccably maintained greens. For much of its history, the course was shared with grazing sheep—a tradition that only ended in the 1970s—giving it a rugged, authentic character. Notable for its challenging par-threes and significant elevation changes, Sanquhar offers a spirited test of golf. It is a traditional club that represents the backbone of Scottish village golf: historic, community-focused, and deeply integrated into the local landscape.

Scoonie
Scoonie Golf Club is a beautiful 18-hole municipal course located in the seaside town of Leven, Fife. While it sits near the famous Leven Links, Scoonie offers a distinct parkland challenge. The course was significantly redesigned in 1936 by the legendary James Braid, who brought his signature strategic bunkering and multi-tiered green designs to the layout. It is characterized by its rolling terrain and the Scoonie Burn, which acts as a natural hazard on several holes.

The club has a vibrant membership and is a favorite for local golfers who appreciate the high-quality conditioning and the fast-draining turf. Notable for its "Braid" influence, the course requires a thoughtful approach to avoid the deep bunkers and tricky slopes. It offers panoramic views over the Firth of Forth and is widely considered one of the best-value municipal courses in the country. Scoonie provides a polished, professional, and accessible parkland experience in one of the world's most iconic golfing regions.

Scotscraig
Scotscraig Golf Club is a world-class championship venue and the 13th oldest golf club in the world, founded in 1817 by members of the St Andrews Society of Golfers. The layout is a unique "links-heathland" hybrid, featuring the firm turf of a links course but with gorse and heather-lined fairways more typical of an inland track. Designed by the "Grand Masters" Old Tom Morris and James Braid, it has served as a Final Qualifying venue for the Open Championship for decades.

The course is legendary for its small, firm greens and its demanding strategic layout. Notable players who have tackled Scotscraig during Open qualifying include Justin Rose, Ernie Els, and Lee Westwood. It is a prestigious, traditional club where the standards of play and maintenance are among the highest in Scotland. To play Scotscraig is to experience a masterclass in golf architecture; it is an unforgiving, historic, and beautifully presented test of the game that remains a mandatory stop for any serious golfer visiting Fife.

Seafield
Seafield Golf Course is the "little sister" to the championship Belleisle course in Ayr. Designed by the legendary James Braid and opened in 1927, Seafield is a shorter, more accessible layout that still features the strategic hallmarks of a Braid design. It is a parkland-links hybrid that runs closer to the shoreline than Belleisle, offering a variety of holes that transition from sheltered woodland to exposed coastal terrain.

Despite its shorter yardage, Seafield is notoriously tricky, with small greens and narrow fairways that punish the over-ambitious driver. It is maintained to the same high standards as its famous neighbor and is a favorite for those looking for a quick but technically demanding round. The club features a state-of-the-art £1.6 million clubhouse shared with Belleisle. Seafield represents the perfect balance of challenge and charm, providing a high-value golfing experience on the famous Ayrshire coast.

Selkirk
Selkirk Golf Club is a "wee gem" of a course perched on the hills overlooking the historic Borders town. Established in 1883, the current layout was designed in 1924 by the great Willie Park Jr. (architect of Sunningdale Old). It is a 9-hole moorland course that offers some of the most spectacular views in the Southern Uplands, stretching across the Linglie Hills toward the Ettrick and Yarrow valleys.

The course is famous for its "hill turf"—firm, springy, and remarkably fast-draining. It is an "honesty box" facility that maintains a traditional, unpretentious atmosphere. Notable for its thick heather and the "Long Hole" (the 8th), which requires two perfect shots to reach a hidden green, Selkirk is a tactical test of the highest order. It is a peaceful, scenic, and spiritually uplifting place to play, offering a pure connection to the game's 19th-century moorland roots.

Shetland
Shetland Golf Club, located just outside Lerwick, is the most northerly golf course in the UK. Originally based on the Isle of Bressay, the club moved to its current site at Dale in the 1970s. This 18-hole moorland course is an elemental experience, where the lack of trees means the golfer is entirely exposed to the North Atlantic winds. The layout is rugged and undulating, featuring natural water hazards and the constant presence of the surrounding hills and sea.

The club is a focal point of the Shetland community and is known for its incredibly warm and welcoming atmosphere. Notable for its "Midnight Sun" tournaments in June, where golf is played through the night in the northern "simmer dim" the course offers an experience unlike any other in the world. It is a place where you must "play the ground" utilizing the contours to navigate the wind. For the adventurous traveler, Shetland Golf Club provides a raw, beautiful, and unforgettable golfing frontier.

Shiskine
Shiskine Golf & Tennis Club on the Isle of Arran is a global icon and arguably the best 12-hole course in the world. Founded in 1896 and designed by Willie Fernie and Willie Park Jr., the course was originally 18 holes, but six were lost to neglect during WWI. Rather than rebuild them, the club kept the 12 best holes, creating a unique and thrilling "roller-coaster" of a round. It is set against the dramatic backdrop of the Drumadoon Cliffs and the Kilbrannan Sound.

The course is famous for its quirks, including several blind shots and the iconic "Crow's Nest" (the 3rd), a par-three played straight up a cliff face. Notable for its "pure fun" factor, Shiskine is a site of pilgrimage for golfers from across the globe. It is an unpretentious, friendly club where the joy of the game takes precedence over a formal scorecard. To play Shiskine is to rediscover why we love golf—it is creative, breathtakingly scenic, and completely unique.

Shotts
Shotts Golf Club is a rugged and challenging moorland course situated on the high plateau of North Lanarkshire. Established in 1923, the course was designed by the legendary James Braid, who expertly utilized the natural peat and heather of the landscape to create a stern test of golf. Sitting 800 feet above sea level, the course offers panoramic views that, on a clear day, stretch across the Forth Valley to the peaks of the Ochil Hills.


The club is known for its resilient, "all-weather" membership and its remarkably fast-draining turf. Notable for its exposure to the winds, Shotts requires a low, stinging ball flight and a creative short game. It has a prestigious history in the Lanarkshire amateur circuit and is praised for its consistent conditioning. The signature 4th hole, "The Spectacles" features two cavernous bunkers that demand a precise carry. It is an honest, traditional club that offers a spirited and physically engaging round of golf, capturing the raw essence of Scottish moorland play.

Silverknowes
Silverknowes Golf Course is a premier municipal links-parkland hybrid located on the shores of the Firth of Forth in Edinburgh. Designed by James Braid and opened in the 1930s, the course offers a high-quality, accessible challenge that has long been a favorite for the city's residents. The layout is relatively flat and open, but its primary defense is the unpredictable sea breeze that whips across the exposed fairways.

As one of the busiest municipal courses in Scotland, Silverknowes has served as a training ground for thousands of golfers. It has hosted various Lothians County amateur events and is highly regarded for the quality of its greens. The course offers stunning views across to the island of Cramond and the mountains of Fife. Notable for its friendly and bustling atmosphere, Silverknowes provides a "proper" links-style test at an affordable price, representing the democratic spirit of the game in the heart of the capital.

Skeabost
Skeabost Golf Club on the Isle of Skye is a hidden gem in the truest sense, offering a tranquil and atmospheric 9-hole experience. Situated in the grounds of the historic Skeabost House Hotel, the course winds along the banks of the River Snizort. It is a scenic parkland-moorland hybrid characterized by its lush greenery and the dramatic backdrop of the Skye hills. The river acts as a natural hazard on several holes, requiring a steady nerve on the approach shots.

The club is known for its relaxed, "boutique" atmosphere, making it a favorite for visitors looking to combine a Highland holiday with a peaceful round of golf. While it lacks the length of a championship course, it is technically demanding, with small, well-protected greens. Notable for its salmon-filled river and its diverse wildlife, Skeabost offers a "slow-golf" experience where the beauty of the surroundings is the primary attraction. It is a quiet, soulful place to play, representing the intimate and natural side of island golf.

Skelmorlie
Skelmorlie Golf Club is a spectacular 13-hole moorland course perched on the hills high above the Firth of Clyde. Established in 1891, the course is famous for its panoramic views that stretch from the island of Bute to the mountains of Argyll. Because it consists of 13 holes, a "full" round involves repeating five holes from different tees to create an 18-hole loop. The layout is a physical test, featuring significant elevation changes and rugged, natural hazards.

The club is a focal point of the local community and is known for its warm, unpretentious welcome. Braid's influence (who advised on the layout in the early 20th century) is evident in the strategic positioning of holes along the ridges. Notable for its springy turf and its exposure to the sea gales, Skelmorlie offers an exhilarating and varied challenge. The signature view from the clubhouse balcony over the estuary is worth the visit alone. It is a traditional club that provides high-value golf with one of the most cinematic backdrops in the West of Scotland.

Southerness
Southerness Golf Club is a world-class links located on the remote Solway Coast, designed by the esteemed Philip Mackenzie Ross in 1947. It is frequently ranked as one of the top ten courses in Scotland and is a masterpiece of traditional links design. The course is situated on a coastal plain with no trees to speak of, meaning the golfer is entirely at the mercy of the wind. It has hosted the Scottish Amateur Championship and several prestigious international matches.

The layout is characterized by its deep, sod-walled bunkers, narrow fairways, and fast-running turf. Notable for its isolation and its stunning views across the Solway Firth to the English Lake District, Southerness offers a "pure" links experience that feels entirely secluded from the modern world. The greens are famously firm and fast, requiring a delicate touch. It is a prestigious and welcoming club that prides itself on maintaining a championship-standard course that tests every facet of a player's skill. To play Southerness is to experience one of the great, unsung icons of Scottish golf.

South Ronaldsay
South Ronaldsay Golf Club is a charming and elemental 9-hole links-moorland hybrid located on the southernmost island of the Orkney archipelago. Established in 1993, the course is a testament to community spirit, having been built and maintained by local volunteers. It is situated on high ground overlooking the Pentland Firth, providing spectacular views toward the Scottish mainland and the distant peaks of Caithness.

The club is an "honesty box" facility and is known for its incredibly relaxed and friendly atmosphere. While it lacks a professional architect, the routing is clever, utilizing the natural slopes and rocky outcrops to create a variety of challenging shots. The wind is a constant factor here, often turning a short par-four into a daunting test of endurance. Notable for its tranquility and its connection to the local landscape, South Ronaldsay offers a raw and authentic northern golfing experience. It is a hidden treasure for those who enjoy the simple, unadorned pleasure of the game in a wild and beautiful setting.

Spean Bridge
Spean Bridge Golf Club is a scenic 9-hole parkland course located in the heart of the Great Glen, just north of Fort William. Established in 1905, the course offers some of the most dramatic mountain views in the country, sitting in the shadow of the mighty Ben Nevis. The layout is relatively flat and winds through mature trees and along the banks of the River Spean, which provides a natural hazard on several holes.

The club is a vibrant hub for the local community and is known for its warm, Highland hospitality. While it is a shorter course, it requires a high degree of accuracy to navigate the narrow fairways and avoid the lush vegetation. Notable for its peaceful, secluded atmosphere and its proximity to the Commando Memorial, Spean Bridge is a favorite for tourists and locals alike. The greens are remarkably true for such an exposed site. It is an honest, traditional club that provides a tranquil and high-value round of golf, capturing the rugged, green spirit of the Highlands.

Spey Bay
Spey Bay Golf Club is a rugged and traditional links course situated at the mouth of the River Spey on the Moray coast. Designed by the legendary Ben Sayers in 1907, the course is a "hidden" links of exceptional quality. It is characterized by its firm, sandy turf, gorse-lined fairways, and the ever-present threat of the North Sea wind. The course recently came under new ownership (the owners of Cabot Saint Lucia) and is undergoing a high-profile renovation to return it to its former glory.

The layout is a classic "out and back" links that rewards creative shot-making and a low ball flight. Notable for its incredible wildlife, including dolphins and seals often visible from the shore, Spey Bay offers a sense of total immersion in nature. While it hasn't hosted the major pro tours, it is a stalwart of the Northern amateur circuit. The signature holes along the pebble beach are both beautiful and treacherous. It is a welcoming, unpretentious club that offers a raw, atmospheric, and spiritually moving round of links golf in a stunningly wild location.

Spey Valley
Spey Valley Golf Club in Aviemore is a modern championship masterpiece located within the Cairngorms National Park. Designed by the renowned Dave Thomas and opened in 2006, it is one of the longest courses in Scotland, measuring over 7,100 yards from the back tees. The layout is a spectacular parkland-heathland hybrid that winds through ancient Scots pine forests and alongside the River Spey. It is a regular host for the European Challenge Tour's Scottish Hydro Challenge.

The course is famous for its scale and its dramatic scenery, featuring the longest par-five in Scotland (the 5th hole, "The Monster" measuring 635 yards). Notable for its large, undulating greens and strategic water hazards, Spey Valley is a "big" course that rewards power and precision in equal measure. The views of the Cairngorm mountains from every fairway are simply breathtaking. It is a professional, high-gloss resort course that offers a world-class, five-star golfing experience, making it a centerpiece of the Highland golf trail.

St Andrews - Balgove
The Balgove Course at St Andrews is the only 9-hole course at the "Home of Golf" specifically designed to cater to beginners, juniors, and families. While it sits in the shadow of the world-famous Old Course, the Balgove is maintained to the same exacting standards as the rest of the St Andrews Links Trust estate. It features wide fairways and large bunkers, providing a gentle introduction to the unique challenges of links golf.


The course is a vital part of the St Andrews community, serving as the primary training ground for the next generation of local golfers. It offers a relaxed and unpretentious environment where the pressure of the championship courses is absent. Notable for its accessibility and its perfectly manicured turf, the Balgove allows players to experience the "magic" of St Andrews without the daunting difficulty of the larger tracks. It is the perfect venue for a fun, stress-free "nine" in the heart of the world's most famous golfing town, proving that golf for all is a core value of the Links Trust.

St Andrews - Castle
The Castle Course is the newest addition to the St Andrews Links Trust, opened in 2008 and designed by David McLay Kidd (the architect of Bandon Dunes). Perched on a rugged cliff-top overlooking the town, it offers a starkly different experience from the traditional links below. It is famous for its massive, rolling undulations and some of the most complex greens in the country. The layout is a visual masterpiece, with the North Sea visible from every hole and the skyline of St Andrews providing a dramatic backdrop.

The course has hosted the European Tour's St Andrews Bay Championship and is a favorite for those seeking a "modern-traditional" challenge. Notable for its 17th hole, a par-three requiring a heroic carry over a yawning chasm of sea and rock, it is a course that demands imagination and a steady nerve. While controversial when it first opened due to its difficulty, it has matured into a prestigious and exhilarating round that provides a thrilling, elevated contrast to the classic seaside tracks of the Auld Grey Toon.

St Andrews - Craigtoun (The Duke's)
The Duke's Course, located on the high ground overlooking St Andrews, is the only parkland layout in the town. Originally designed by Peter Thomson (five-time Open winner) and later significantly revised by Tim Liddy in 2006, the course offers a "resort-style" experience of the highest caliber. It is characterized by its wide-open spaces, rugged bunkering, and a "heathland" feel that provides a beautiful alternative to the coastal links.

Owned by the Old Course Hotel, The Duke's has hosted the European Amateur Championship and is a regular venue for elite international events. Notable for its expansive views of the town and the sea, it is a "big" course that rewards powerful driving and strategic approach play. The greens are large and fast, and the gorse-lined fairways provide a colorful Highland-edge atmosphere. It is a polished, professional, and tranquil sanctuary that offers a world-class inland round in the world's most famous golfing destination.

St Andrews - Eden
The Eden Course was opened in 1914 to ease the pressure on the Old and New courses, designed by the legendary Harry Colt. Colt brought his signature strategic bunkering to the links, creating a layout that is shorter than its neighbors but arguably more technical. It is characterized by its small, well-guarded greens and several significant water hazards, including the Eden Estuary which comes into play on the early holes.

The club has a vibrant social scene and is a favorite for local medals and visiting societies. Notable for its "traditional links" feel without the intimidating length of a championship track, the Eden requires a high degree of accuracy off the tee. It has hosted various Scottish regional tournaments and remains a vital part of the St Andrews Links Trust estate. It is the perfect course for the "thinking" golfer who appreciates the subtleties of Colt's design and wants to experience the magic of St Andrews in a slightly more relaxed environment.

St Andrews - Jubilee
The Jubilee Course is often cited by locals as the most difficult of all the St Andrews links.
