Originally opened in 1897 to commemorate Queen Victoria's Diamond Jubilee, it was a 12-hole course before being extended and eventually redesigned in 1988 by Donald Steel into a championship-standard links. It is situated on the narrowest strip of land between the New Course and the sea, featuring deep dunes and narrow fairways.

The course has hosted numerous amateur championships and is a regular test for the St Andrews Links Trophy. Notable for its relentless demand for accuracy, especially when the wind whips off the West Sands, the Jubilee provides a "pure" links experience that many believe is a truer test of skill than its more famous neighbors. The elevated tees offer stunning views of the estuary and the town. It is a rugged, uncompromising, and beautifully maintained track that represents the very best of modern links architecture in a historic setting.

St Andrews - New
The New Course at St Andrews is only "new" in name—it was actually opened in 1895. Designed by the "Grand Old Man of Golf" Old Tom Morris, it was built to accommodate the increasing demand for golf in the town. It is a classic "out and back" links, running parallel to the Old Course, and many purists consider it a more consistent and "fairer" test than its more famous sibling. It features traditional gorse-lined fairways, deep bunkers, and fast-running turf.

The club has a prestigious history and shares many of the same views and conditions as the Old Course. Notable for its shared fairways and challenging finishing holes, the New Course is a regular venue for national amateur events. It is a favorite for local members who appreciate the logical flow of Old Tom's design. To play the New is to experience the absolute peak of late 19th-century links architecture—it is honest, challenging, and steeped in the traditions of the St Andrews Links Trust.

St Andrews - Old
The Old Course is the undisputed home of golf, the place where the game was born and where every great champion has walked. Its history stretches back over 600 years. Originally a natural progression across the links land, it was refined by Old Tom Morris and Alister MacKenzie. It is home to the most iconic landmarks in the sport: the Swilcan Bridge, the Road Hole (17th), and the massive double greens that span half an acre.

Muirfield may be the most "perfect" design, but the Old Course is the most "magical." It has hosted The Open Championship 30 times, with winners including Tiger Woods, Jack Nicklaus, and Bobby Jones. Notable members include the entire history of the R&A. To play here is a spiritual experience; the sense of history is palpable as you stand on the 1st tee. It is a public course that belongs to the world, offering a unique, strategic, and profoundly moving round of golf that every player dreams of completing once in their lifetime.

St Andrews - Strathtyrum
The Strathtyrum Course was opened in 1993 to provide a more accessible and enjoyable links experience for players of all levels. While it is the shortest of the 18-hole courses at St Andrews, it is maintained to the same high standards as the championship tracks. Designed by Donald Steel, the layout features wider fairways and fewer bunkers, making it an ideal choice for a relaxed round or for those looking to build their confidence on links turf.

The course is particularly popular with families, seniors, and visitors who want to enjoy the St Andrews atmosphere without the brutal challenge of the Jubilee or the Old. Notable for its large, undulating greens that still require a sharp putting stroke, the Strathtyrum offers a scenic and tranquil environment. It provides a vital balance to the Links Trust's portfolio, ensuring that the "Home of Golf" remains a destination for everyone. It is a high-quality, friendly, and beautifully presented course that captures the joy of the game in its purest form.

St Boswells
St Boswells Golf Club is a charming and historic 9-hole parkland course situated on the banks of the River Tweed in the Scottish Borders. Established in 1899, the course is famous for its idyllic setting and its remarkably well-conditioned greens. The layout winds along the riverbank, with the water providing a beautiful but treacherous hazard on several holes. The mature trees and lush vegetation create a peaceful and sheltered environment.

The club is known for its warm Borders hospitality and its vibrant community spirit. While it is a shorter course, the sloping fairways and small greens require a high degree of accuracy and a delicate touch. It has a prestigious history in the Borders Golfers' Association and is a favorite for local society outings. Notable for its "village green" atmosphere and its stunning river views, St Boswells offers a tranquil and high-value round of golf. It is a quintessential Scottish village club—unpretentious, scenic, and deeply traditional—offering a peaceful escape in one of the country's most beautiful regions.

St Fillans
St Fillans Golf Club is a spectacular 9-hole Highland gem located at the eastern end of Loch Earn. Established in 1903 and significantly redesigned in the 1920s by the legendary James Braid, the course is frequently described as one of the most beautiful in Scotland. It is situated in a natural amphitheater of mountains, with the "Bolfracks" hills providing a dramatic backdrop. The course is a parkland-moorland hybrid characterized by its lush greenery and the River Earn, which meanders through the property.

The club has a prestigious connection to the professional game, being the home course of the legendary Sandy Lyle's father, Alex Lyle, who was the professional here for many years. Notable for its peace and seclusion, St Fillans offers a varied and engaging challenge where accuracy is far more important than length. The greens are notoriously true and well-protected. It is a friendly, traditional club that offers a world-class view and a high-quality Braid layout, making it a "must-play" for anyone exploring the heart of Perthshire.

Stirling
Stirling Golf Club is a prestigious parkland course situated in the historic Kings Park, directly below the magnificent Stirling Castle. Established in 1869, the course was redesigned in the 1920s by the prolific James Braid, who created a layout that rewards both power and precision. The course offers panoramic views of the castle, the Wallace Monument, and the distant peaks of the Trossachs. It is a tactical course characterized by its mature trees and strategic bunkering.

The club has a rich history and has hosted many prestigious amateur and professional events, including the Scottish Youths' Championship. Notable members have included local dignitaries and leaders of the central Scotland professional community. The greens at Stirling are famously consistent and fast, requiring a sharp eye for a read. The signature view of the castle from the 1st tee is one of the most iconic sights in Scottish golf. It is a traditional, professional, and welcoming club that offers a polished and historic parkland experience in the "Gateway to the Highlands."

St Medan
St Medan Golf Club is a unique and incredibly scenic 9-hole course located on the shores of Luce Bay in Wigtownshire. Established in 1905, it is famous for its "18 tees to 9 greens" layout, which provides a completely different perspective and challenge on the second loop. The course is situated on a peninsula and is a natural links-style track, where the sea is visible from every hole and the wind is a constant factor.

The club has a special connection to the author Gavin Maxwell (Ring of Bright Water), who grew up in the area; the club even adopted the otter as its logo in his honor. Notable for its family-friendly atmosphere, St Medan celebrated its centenary in 2005. The signature holes require precise shots over rocky inlets and gorse, with the bronze sculpture of Maxwell's otter overlooking the bay from a nearby hill. It is an unpretentious, "slow-golf" gem that offers some of the most tranquil and atmospheric coastal play in the South West.


St Michaels
St Michaels Golf Club, located just outside St Andrews in Fife, is a high-quality parkland-heathland hybrid with a prestigious architectural pedigree. Originally laid out in 1903 by the legendary Old Tom Morris and Hugh Hamilton, the course was extended to 18 holes in 1996, fulfilling the founders' original vision. It is situated on the "Gallow Hill" and its small, firm greens and narrow fairways are often said to be just as testing as those of its famous neighbors in the Auld Grey Toon.


The club is a regular host for Fife County amateur events and is praised for its year-round playability due to its free-draining soil. Notable for its "St Andrews spires" views and its proximity to the River Eden, the course features several standout par-threes. It offers a refined, historic, and more affordable alternative to the Links Trust courses, maintaining a traditional atmosphere where the quality of the conditioning is paramount. St Michaels is a "thinking man's" course that rewards strategy and precision over raw power.


Stonehaven
Stonehaven Golf Club is one of the most dramatic clifftop courses in Scotland, perched on the "Braes of Cowie" overlooking the North Sea. Founded in 1888, the course is unique because it sits directly on the Highland Fault Line, which separates the Highlands from the Lowlands. The layout is characterized by its significant elevation changes and thrilling short holes played over deep, rocky gullies where a mishit ball is lost to the ocean below.


The club is a vibrant part of the Aberdeenshire community and was recently ranked in the Top 100 Scottish Courses by Golf World, described as "brilliant fun." Notable for its views of the historic Dunnottar Castle to the south, the course is relatively short (par 66) but notoriously tricky when the sea breeze picks up. It is a traditional, friendly club that provides an exhilarating and visually stunning round of golf, where the dramatic scenery often compensates for a bruised scorecard.

Stornoway
Stornoway Golf Club, located in the grounds of Lews Castle on the Isle of Lewis, is the premier 18-hole course in the Outer Hebrides. While the club was instituted in 1890—legend suggests it may have been laid out by Old Tom Morris during a "missionary journey" to the islands—the current layout was constructed in 1947 by John R. Stutt. It is a lush, wooded parkland course that provides a stark and beautiful contrast to the rugged moorland and machair links typically found in the Western Isles.


The club is the heart of the Hebridean golfing scene and is known for its incredibly warm island hospitality. Notable for its shelter provided by the castle's mature woodland, it offers a more tranquil playing experience than the wind-blasted coastal tracks. The course has hosted the Western Isles Open and is a regular venue for regional championships. With its panoramic views of Stornoway Harbour and the Minch, it offers a sophisticated and scenic round of golf that highlights the diverse landscape of the Outer Hebrides.

Stranraer
Stranraer Golf Club holds a significant place in history as the final course designed by the legendary James Braid before his death in 1950. Situated on the shores of Loch Ryan, the course is a championship-standard parkland layout that offers spectacular views over the water to Ailsa Craig and the Isle of Arran. Braid utilized the undulating terrain to create a strategic masterpiece that rewards thoughtful positioning off the tee.

The club has a prestigious tournament pedigree, frequently hosting national amateur events and regional PGA Scotland pro-ams. Notable for its lush conditioning and the "Creachmore Burn" that meanders through the property, Stranraer is a "fair" but stern test of golf. The signature 5th hole is often cited as one of the best par-fours in the country. It is a professional and welcoming club that offers a "Tour-standard" experience in a setting of exceptional natural beauty, representing Braid's enduring architectural legacy.

Strathaven
Strathaven Golf Club is a premier parkland course in Lanarkshire, originally laid out as a 9-hole track by the 1883 Open Champion Willie Fernie. It was extended to a full 18 holes in 1965 with design work by John R. Stutt. The course has matured into one of the best parkland venues in the West of Scotland, characterized by its tight, tree-lined fairways and exceptionally well-manicured greens.

The club has a long history of hosting top-tier tournaments, including the 2021 Scottish Girls' Amateur Championship. Notable for its challenging "tunnel" fairways and strategic bunkering, Strathaven is a course that demands accuracy from start to finish. The 16th hole, a 462-yard par-four through mature woodland, is widely considered one of the toughest tests in the region. It is a vibrant, friendly club that offers a polished and high-quality golfing experience just a short drive from Glasgow.

Strathclyde Park
Strathclyde Park Golf Course is a popular 9-hole municipal facility located within the Strathclyde Country Park in Hamilton. The course occupies a unique position, bordered by the Hamilton Racecourse on one side and a nature reserve on the other. It is a classic parkland layout featuring mature woodland and open fairways, providing a gentle but engaging challenge for golfers of all skill levels.

As a municipal facility operated by South Lanarkshire Leisure, it is a vital entry point for the game in the local community. Notable for its proximity to the Strathclyde Park Family Golf Centre, which features a 24-bay floodlit driving range, it offers a comprehensive environment for practice and play. While it doesn't boast a celebrity architect, the course is well-regarded for its condition and its tranquil, green setting. It is the perfect venue for a quick, affordable "nine" in a scenic urban park environment.

Strathendrick
Strathendrick Golf Club is a beautiful and historic 9-hole parkland course situated on the banks of the River Endrick near Killearn. Designed in 1901 by the legendary Willie Fernie, the course is perched on an elevated site that offers breathtaking panoramic views of Ben Lomond, the Luss Hills, and the Campsies. The layout is undulating and features many natural hazards, requiring the use of every club in the bag.


The club is famous for its quaint, 'C' Listed pavilion clubhouse which dates back to the club's founding. Notable for its high-quality fairways and its friendly, welcoming atmosphere, Strathendrick is a favorite for visitors looking for a traditional "village" golfing experience. While it is a shorter course, the varying layout and the presence of the river ensure that it remains a stern test for even expert players. It is a peaceful and scenic gem that captures the lush, green essence of the Stirlingshire countryside.

Strathlene (Buckie)
Strathlene Buckie Golf Club is a historic clifftop links course that dates back to 1877, making it one of the oldest clubs in Scotland. Located on the Moray Firth coast, the course is a unique hybrid that combines ancient links features with modern design elements (it was extended to 18 holes in 1936). The layout is routed around a central dune ridge and features tumultuous terrain, elevated greens, and spectacular sea views.

The course is featured in the book True Links, which catalogues the genuine links courses of the world. Notable for its exposure to the North Sea winds and its challenging gullies and ravines on the closing holes, Strathlene is a "raw" and authentic golfing experience. While the clubhouse is a more modern addition, the turf remains traditional and fast-running. It is a welcoming, unpretentious club that offers a "spectacular and underrated" round of golf on one of the most beautiful stretches of the Moray coastline.

Strathmore Golf Centre
Strathmore Golf Centre, located in the heart of the Strathmore Valley near Alyth, is a premier 27-hole facility that opened in 1996. The main Rannaleroch Course was designed by John Salvesen (a former R&A Captain) and is a championship-standard parkland-heathland hybrid. Known as "The Friendly Place to Play Golf" the centre has won numerous awards, including Scotland's Best Golf Course (Under £75) at the 2022 Scottish Golf Tourism Awards.


The Rannaleroch layout is minimalist in style, working with the natural rolling farmland to create a variety of challenges, including a notable water carry on the par-five 5th hole. The facility also features the 9-hole Leitfie Links, which is ideal for juniors and beginners. Notable for its world-class conditioning and its modern, inclusive atmosphere, Strathmore has quickly become a cornerstone of the Perthshire golf scene. It offers a professional, high-value, and welcoming experience that caters to every level of the game.

Strathpeffer Spa
Strathpeffer Spa Golf Club is frequently hailed as the "hidden gem of the Highlands." Established in 1888, the course was designed by two of the most significant figures in golf history: Willie Park Jr. (the 1887 and 1889 Open Champion) laid out the first nine, and Old Tom Morris completed the 18-hole extension a decade later. Perched on a high ridge overlooking the Victorian spa village, the course offers breathtaking panoramic views over the Cromarty Firth and the peaks of Ben Wyvis.

The club is famous for its extreme elevation changes, providing a physical and tactical challenge. Notable for its natural, rugged conditioning, the layout feels like a step back into the late 19th century. Legendary commentator Peter Alliss famously praised its scenic beauty. While the course is relatively short, its defense lies in the undulating terrain and small, tricky greens. It is a traditional and welcoming club that offers a "venerable" golfing experience where you can walk the same fairways as the founders of the professional game.

Strathtay
Strathtay Golf Club is a picturesque and tranquil 9-hole parkland course set in the heart of Highland Perthshire. Originally laid out in 1909 by Captain Steuart of Ballechin, the course remained largely unchanged for a century until nine additional tees were added in 2008 to celebrate its centenary. This "9 holes, 18 tees" layout provides a varied experience, with the elevated tees offering stunning vistas of the Tay Valley and the surrounding peaks.

The club is known for its peaceful environment and the exceptional condition of its greens. Each tee marker provides a small snippet of the club's history, making a round here a delightful journey through time. Notable for its lush fairways and mature woodland, Strathendrick offers a classic "village" golf experience. It is a friendly, community-focused club that prides itself on its inclusive atmosphere, making it a favorite for both locals and visitors looking for a high-quality, stress-free round in a world-class landscape.

Stromness
Stromness Golf Club, founded in 1890, is a unique and imaginative seaside parkland course located at the southern entrance to the historic Orkney harbor town. The course offers spectacular views across to the islands of Hoy and Graemsay, as well as the world-famous Scapa Flow. One of its most distinctive features is that the routing actually takes players over and around WWII gun emplacements and underground bunkers, serving as a living memorial to the region's strategic military history.

While relatively short (just over 4,800 yards), the tight and tricky layout provides a stern test of accuracy. Notable for its "turn up and play" policy, the club is known for its incredibly relaxed and friendly atmosphere. The course is a focal point for the local community and is particularly scenic during the "simmer dim" (the long Northern summer twilight). It is a "must-play" for those visiting Orkney, offering a blend of sport, history, and stunning maritime scenery that is truly one-of-a-kind.

Swanston
Swanston Golf Club, located at the foot of the Pentland Hills in Edinburgh, has a fascinating history—it was founded in 1927 as a ladies-only course. Due to high demand from the members' husbands, it was soon opened to men and expanded to 18 holes. The course underwent a major modernization in 2006 and further improved in 2016 by incorporating two spectacular holes from the defunct Lothianburn course. The result is a challenging, hilly parkland-moorland hybrid with panoramic views over the city of Edinburgh and the Firth of Forth.

The club has a professional and forward-thinking atmosphere, featuring a world-class academy and a modern, family-friendly clubhouse. Notable for its high-quality conditioning and its commitment to junior development, Swanston is a regular host for regional amateur championships. It is a favorite for those seeking a physically engaging round with a "countryside" feel just minutes from the city center. It is a traditional club with a modern outlook, providing a polished and scenic golfing experience in the shadow of the Pentlands.

Swanston Templar Course
The Templar Course at Swanston is a dedicated 9-hole par-three course that serves as the "nursery" for the club's thriving academy. Named after the Knights Templar (who had strong historical ties to the nearby area), the course was built to provide a high-quality environment for beginners, juniors, and those looking to refine their short game. Despite its shorter yardage, the course features tour-standard greens and strategic bunkering that reflect the challenges found on the main 18-hole track.

The Templar is maintained with the same meticulous care as the championship course, ensuring a high-quality experience for all users. It is a vital asset for the Swanston Golf Academy, which is one of the premier teaching facilities in the Lothians. Notable for its inclusive atmosphere and its role in growing the game, the course offers a quick and enjoyable "nine" that is perfect for a post-work round. It represents the club's dedication to accessibility, making golf at the foot of the Pentlands an option for players of all skill levels.

Tain
Tain Golf Club is a "Northern Jewel" designed by the legendary Old Tom Morris in 1890. Situated on the shores of the Dornoch Firth, it is an 18-hole links course that offers a subtle and challenging masterpiece of early architecture. It is famously the neighbor of Royal Dornoch, and many golfers consider the two courses to be the perfect "Highland double." Tain is characterized by its firm, sandy turf, gorse-lined fairways, and the "Alps" hole (the 11th), where a blind approach is played over a massive ridge.

The club has a prestigious history and has hosted the Scottish Women's Championship and the Columbo Cup (since 1897). Notable for its proximity to the Glenmorangie Distillery, the course offers a sensory experience of sea air and malt whisky. The 17th hole, "Black Bridge" features a meandering river that adds a dramatic water hazard to the final stretch. Tain is a refined, historic, and incredibly welcoming club that offers world-class links golf with a fraction of the crowds found on the more famous Open tracks.

Tarbert
Tarbert Golf Club is a delightful and friendly 9-hole course located in the picturesque village of Tarbert, Argyll. Established in 1898, the course has occupied several sites before settling into its current hilltop location in the 1930s. Originally laid out by the 1883 Open Champion Willie Fernie, the course is a moorland-parkland hybrid that offers stunning views of the surrounding hills and the sea.

The club is known for its unpretentious "honesty box" atmosphere and its incredibly warm welcome for visitors. While the course is short, its defense lies in the narrow fairways and the significant elevation changes that require precise club selection. Notable for its peaceful, secluded setting, Tarbert is a quintessential "Argyll gem" where the focus is on the simple enjoyment of the game. It is the perfect venue for those looking to experience the rugged beauty of the West Coast in a relaxed and traditional setting.

Tarland
Tarland Golf Club is an enchanting 9-hole parkland masterpiece located in the heart of Royal Deeside. Founded in 1908 and designed by the legendary Old Tom Morris, the course is often described as a "centennial jewel." It is meticulously maintained and features a layout that rewards accuracy over length. The signature view from the 8th fairway offers a panoramic vista across the Dee Valley to the majestic Lochnagar mountain.

The club is a focal point of the local community and is known for its traditional Scottish hospitality. While a 9-hole track, the use of multiple tees for a "medal" 18-hole round provides a varied and challenging test. Notable for its lush, wooded environment and its serene atmosphere, Tarland has won numerous awards for its conditioning and value. It is a "must-visit" for anyone touring the Aberdeenshire Highlands, offering a pure connection to the architectural legacy of Tom Morris in a setting of exceptional natural beauty.

Taynuilt
Taynuilt Golf Club is a spectacular 9-hole parkland course situated on the shores of Loch Etive, dominated by the towering peak of Ben Cruachan. Established in 1987 and officially opened in 1991 by the legendary Sir Michael Bonallack, the course has quickly gained a reputation as one of the best 9-hole tracks in the country. The layout is undulating and winds along the banks of the River Nant, which frames the final hole.

The club is known for its friendly, "volunteer-run" spirit and its remarkably well-conditioned turf. Notable for its picture-postcard views, Taynuilt offers a challenging round where the small greens and natural water hazards keep players on their toes. It is a regular host for the Argyll and Bute regional championships. For those traveling through the West Highlands, Taynuilt provides a peaceful and visually stunning golfing sanctuary that captures the green, rugged spirit of the landscape.

The Renaissance Club
The Renaissance Club in East Lothian is one of the most prestigious modern additions to the "Home of Golf." Established in 2008 and designed by the acclaimed Tom Doak, it is a world-class links that blends contemporary luxury with traditional architectural values. Since 2019, the club has been the permanent home of the Scottish Open, hosting the world's best players, including Rory McIlroy and Xander Schauffele.

The course is a tactical masterpiece, featuring Doak's signature large, undulating greens and strategic bunkering that utilizes the natural landscape. The "cliff-edge" stretch (holes 9 through 11) offers breathtaking views of the Firth of Forth. Notable for its exclusive atmosphere and its "Tour-standard" conditioning, The Renaissance Club represents the pinnacle of modern Scottish golf. While it is a private club, it offers limited visitor access, providing a rare opportunity to play a course that has become a cornerstone of the professional international circuit.

Thomas Muir (Bishopbriggs)
Thomas Muir Golf Course, often referred to as Bishopbriggs Golf Club, is a premier parkland course located on the northern edge of Glasgow. Established in 1906, the course was designed by the legendary James Braid, who utilized the naturally undulating terrain to create a strategic masterpiece. The layout is characterized by its lush, mature tree-line and several significant water hazards that provide a peaceful and sheltered environment.

The club has a prestigious history and has produced many fine amateur players who have represented Lanarkshire at the highest levels. Notable for its impeccably fast greens and its challenging par-fours, Thomas Muir is a regular host for regional county championships. The signature view of the Campsie Fells from the higher holes is one of the most iconic sights in Glasgow golf. It is a refined, traditional club that prioritizes the quality of its turf and the traditions of the game, offering an uncompromising parkland test that remains a favorite for the city's golfing community.

Thornton
Thornton Golf Club is a beautiful parkland gem located in the heart of Fife, established in 1921. The course is situated on the banks of the River Ore, which acts as a natural and often treacherous hazard on several holes. The layout is characterized by its mature woodland and remarkably flat terrain, making it an easy and enjoyable walk for golfers of all ages. Despite its lack of elevation, Thornton is notoriously tricky, with narrow fairways and well-protected greens.

The club is a focal point of the local community and is known for its warm, Fife hospitality. While it doesn't host professional tours, it has a reputation for being one of the best-maintained inland tracks in the county. Notable for its peaceful, secluded atmosphere and its diverse wildlife, Thornton offers a "hidden" golfing experience away from the busy coastal links. The 18th hole, playing back toward the traditional clubhouse, provides a classic finish. It is a friendly, unpretentious club that offers a high-value and technically demanding round of golf in a tranquil setting.

Thurso
Thurso Golf Club holds the distinction of being the most northerly golf course on the British mainland. Established in 1893, the course offers a rugged and atmospheric moorland-links hybrid experience. The layout is perched on high ground overlooking the town and the Pentland Firth, providing spectacular views toward the Orkney Isles and the towering cliffs of Dunnet Head.

The club is a vital part of the Caithness community and is known for its incredibly warm and unpretentious welcome. While it lacks a "celebrity" architect, the natural routing is a masterclass in utilizing the wind-swept landscape to create a variety of challenging shots. Notable for its firm, springy turf and its exposure to the fierce Atlantic gales, Thurso requires a creative array of "low-ball" shots. It is an "honesty box" facility that represents the very soul of northern golf—wild, scenic, and deeply connected to the elements. For those traveling the North Coast 500, Thurso is an essential and spiritually moving stop.

Tillicoultry
Tillicoultry Golf Club is a spectacular and historic 9-hole moorland course situated on the slopes of the Ochil Hills. Established in 1899, the course offers panoramic views across the Forth Valley to the peaks of the Southern Uplands. It is a "mountain-style" layout characterized by steep climbs and thrilling downhill shots, requiring a good level of fitness and a creative approach to the various blind shots.

The club is known for its friendly, community-focused atmosphere and its traditional clubhouse. While it is a shorter course, the natural hazards of heather and gorse, combined with the significant elevation changes, ensure that it remains a stern test for even expert players. Notable for its peaceful, elevated setting, Tillicoultry provides a spirited and challenging round of golf that captures the rugged beauty of the Stirlingshire countryside. It is an honest, traditional club that offers high-value golf with a view that is truly breathtaking.

Tobermory
Tobermory Golf Club on the Isle of Mull is frequently described as one of the most scenic 9-hole courses in the world. Established in 1896, the course is perched on the cliffs high above the iconic colorful harbor of Tobermory. The layout is a rugged moorland hybrid that offers breathtaking views across the Sound of Mull to the mountains of Ardnamurchan. It is a physical test, featuring significant elevation changes and natural hazards like rocky outcrops and thick heather.

The club is known for its incredibly relaxed, "island-style" hospitality and its "honesty box" policy. While it lacks the length of a championship course, it is technically demanding, with small greens nestled into the hillside. Notable for its peace and seclusion, Tobermory offers a "slow-golf" experience where the beauty of the surroundings is the primary attraction. It is a quiet, soulful place to play, representing the intimate and natural side of Hebridean golf. To play here is to experience the game as it was over a century ago—simple, beautiful, and completely unique.

Torrance House
Torrance House Golf Club is a premier 18-hole municipal parkland course located in East Kilbride, Lanarkshire. Developed in the 1960s around the historic 17th-century Torrance House, the course has matured into a scenic and testing facility. The layout winds through mature woodland and features several significant elevation changes, providing a varied and engaging challenge. It has a strong competitive history and frequently hosts Lanarkshire County amateur events.


As a municipal facility, Torrance House is known for its inclusive and friendly atmosphere. While it is a relatively long course, it is an easy walk and offers wide fairways that encourage bold driving. Notable for its impeccably fast greens and its strategic bunkering, it is widely considered one of the best-value public courses in the country. The signature view of the historic house from the 18th fairway provides a dramatic finish to the round. It is a cherished community asset that represents the "people's game" in a setting of exceptional natural beauty.

Torphins
Torphins Golf Club is a charming and historic 9-hole parkland-moorland hybrid located in the heart of Royal Deeside. Established in 1896, the course is perched on a hillside overlooking the village and the surrounding Aberdeenshire hills. The layout is characterized by its significant elevation changes and its lush, well-manicured fairways. The surrounding woodland and the backdrop of the Grampian mountains provide a tranquil and stunning setting for a round of golf.

The club is a vital part of the local community and is known for its warm, Deeside hospitality. While it is a shorter course, it requires a high degree of accuracy to navigate the sloping fairways and small, tricky greens. Notable for its peaceful, secluded atmosphere and its commitment to traditional values, Torphins offers a "boutique" golfing experience that captures the natural beauty of the region. It is the perfect venue for those looking for a quick, scenic, and high-value round of golf in one of Scotland's most beautiful and historic valleys.

Torvean
Torvean Golf Club in Inverness underwent a major transformation in 2019, moving to a spectacular new 18-hole championship-standard parkland layout. Designed to provide a modern and high-quality experience, the course is situated on the hills overlooking the Caledonian Canal and the Great Glen. The layout features wide, rolling fairways, strategic water hazards, and large, subtly undulating greens that reflect the best of contemporary golf design.

The club has a vibrant and professional atmosphere, frequently hosting regional Highland amateur championships. Notable for its "Tour-standard" practice facilities and its modern, inclusive clubhouse, Torvean has quickly become a premier destination for golfers visiting the capital of the Highlands. The signature holes overlooking the canal provide a unique and scenic backdrop to the round. It is a polished, high-gloss club that offers a modern and engaging golfing experience, perfect for those who appreciate contemporary design and world-class maintenance in a historic Highland setting.

Traigh
Traigh Golf Club is often cited as the most beautiful 9-hole course in Scotland. Located on the "Road to the Isles" near Arisaig, the course is situated on a series of sandy dunes overlooking the white beaches of Traigh and the islands of Rum, Eigg, and Muck. Established in 1900 and redesigned in the 1990s by John Salvesen, the layout is a natural links masterpiece that flows seamlessly with the rugged coastline.

The club is known for its incredibly relaxed atmosphere and its stunning sunsets. While it is a shorter course, the wind off the Atlantic and the natural hazards of the dunes ensure that it remains a stern test of skill. Notable for its isolation and its cinematic views, Traigh offers a raw, elemental connection to the origins of the game. To play here is to rediscover why we love golf—it is creative, breathtakingly scenic, and spiritually moving. It is a "must-visit" for any adventurous golfer traveling through the West Highlands.

Trowan (The Lost Course)
Trowan is a fascinating "lost" course located near Crieff in Perthshire. Originally a 9-hole track laid out in the late 19th century, it was a victim of the mid-20th century decline in local village clubs. However, the site remains a point of historical interest for golf architecture enthusiasts. The natural routing can still be traced across the undulating moorland, showing how early designers used the rocky outcrops and natural burns as organic hazards.

While you cannot play a formal round at Trowan today, the area remains a beautiful spot for walking and reflects the "ghosts" of Scotland's golfing past. It serves as a reminder of a time when almost every village had its own unique course integrated into the local landscape. For those interested in the archaeology of the game, a visit to the Trowan site offers a poignant look at the evolution and occasional disappearance of rural Scottish golf. It represents the "hidden" history of the sport, where the land itself tells the story of generations of forgotten golfers.

Trump International Golf Links
Located at Balmedie in Aberdeenshire, Trump International is one of the most talked-about modern courses in the world. Designed by Dr. Martin Hawtree and opened in 2012, it is a massive, spectacular links built amidst some of the tallest sand dunes in Europe. The course is a "modern-traditional" masterpiece where every hole is secluded from the others by towering ridges of marram grass. It has quickly become a mainstay for elite events and is often cited for its "Tour-standard" conditioning.


The course is notorious for its difficulty, especially when the North Sea wind channels through the valleys. Notable for its 14th hole, which offers a panoramic view of the coastline, and its "Great Dunes" it is a visual and physical test of the highest order. The club features a luxurious, five-star clubhouse and a world-class practice facility. While it is a relatively new addition to the Scottish landscape, it has already established itself as a world-ranking titan that demands every shot in a golfer's bag.


Turnberry - Ailsa
The Ailsa Course at Turnberry is a global icon and a four-time host of The Open Championship. Originally designed by Willie Fernie and famously redesigned after WWII by Mackenzie Ross, it underwent a massive restoration by Martin Ebert in 2016. The "new" Ailsa is widely considered the best course in the UK, featuring a world-famous stretch of holes (6 through 11) that hug the rugged coastline around the iconic Turnberry Lighthouse.


The course was the site of the legendary 1977 "Duel in the Sun" between Jack Nicklaus and Tom Watson. Notable for its 9th hole—now a spectacular par-three played over the ocean to a green at the foot of the lighthouse—it is a breathtaking journey through golf history. The Ailsa is a pure links that offers a refined, luxurious, and spiritually moving experience. To play here is to walk the hallowed ground where the greatest champions have secured their legacy against the backdrop of Ailsa Craig.

Turnberry - King Robert the Bruce
The King Robert the Bruce Course is the spectacular sibling to the Ailsa at the Turnberry Resort. Replaced the old Kintyre course in 2017, this layout was designed by Martin Ebert to provide a championship-standard challenge that complements the main track. It is situated on higher ground, offering expansive views over the Ailsa Course, the lighthouse, and the Irish Sea. The layout features rugged bunkers, native grasses, and several "infinity" greens that seem to blend into the ocean.

Named after the Scottish King who was born at Turnberry Castle, the course is a tribute to the region's history. Notable for its challenging back nine that winds through spectacular coastal terrain, it is a "fair" but formidable links. It is maintained to the same five-star standard as the Ailsa, providing a polished and high-gloss experience. For many golfers, "The Bruce" is a more accessible but equally scenic alternative to its world-famous neighbor, representing the absolute pinnacle of modern links restoration.

Turnhouse
Turnhouse Golf Club is a premier parkland course located on the western outskirts of Edinburgh, near the airport. Established in 1897, the course was significantly redesigned by the legendary James Braid in the 1920s. It is characterized by its rolling terrain, which offers panoramic views of the Fife hills and the Pentland Hills. The layout is famously "breezy" due to its elevated position, making the wind a constant and shifting factor.

The club has a strong competitive history and has produced several Scottish international players. Notable for its impeccably fast greens and its challenging "short" holes, Turnhouse is a regular host for the Lothians County Championships. The course features a variety of tree-lined and open fairways, requiring a versatile approach to shot-making. It is a friendly, professional club that offers a high-quality "city-fringe" golfing experience, making it one of the most popular and respected parkland venues in the capital.

Tyninghame (The Glen)
Tyninghame, often referred to as The Glen (not to be confused with North Berwick's Glen Course), is a hidden links gem located on the John Muir Way in East Lothian. While the historic estate has ancient ties, the modern course is a private and exclusive enclave known for its natural beauty and tranquility. It is a "pure" links characterized by its firm turf, sandy dunes, and stunning views over Belhaven Bay and the Bass Rock.

The course is widely regarded as one of the best-kept secrets in the "Cradle of Golf." Notable for its isolation and its peaceful, natural environment, it offers a "step back in time" experience away from the crowds of the more famous East Lothian tracks. While access is more restricted than the public links, those who play here are rewarded with world-class turf and a layout that follows the organic contours of the shoreline. It is a sanctuary of traditional values, offering a serene and high-quality round of golf in a spectacular coastal setting.

Uig
Uig Golf Club is a rugged and charming 9-hole moorland-links hybrid located on the Isle of Lewis in the Outer Hebrides. Established in the late 20th century, the course is situated on the machair land overlooking the spectacular Uig Bay—famous as the discovery site of the 12th-century Lewis Chessmen. It is a "natural" course in the truest sense, where the hazards consist of sand dunes, wildflowers, and the unpredictable Atlantic wind.

The club is a focal point for the local island community and is known for its incredibly relaxed "honesty box" atmosphere. While it lacks a professional designer, the routing follows the ancient contours of the coast, providing a raw and authentic links experience. Playing Uig is as much about the environment as the sport; it is a place of total silence, interrupted only by the sea and the birds. For the adventurous golfer, it offers a rare opportunity to play the game in a setting of haunting northern beauty and historical significance.

Ullapool
Ullapool Golf Club is a spectacular and scenic 9-hole parkland-links hybrid located on the shores of Loch Broom in the Highlands. Established in 1998 and officially opened by the legendary Prince Andrew, the course offers some of the most dramatic mountain and sea views in the country. The layout is relatively flat and winds along the shoreline, featuring springy turf and several challenging water hazards provided by the loch.

The club is known for its warm, Highland hospitality and its impeccably maintained greens. Notable for its "Midnight Sun" tournaments in June, where golf is played in the long northern twilight, the course offers a unique and memorable experience. It is a favorite for those traveling the North Coast 500 who want a quick, high-quality round in a world-class setting. Ullapool represents the best of modern Highland golf—accessible, scenic, and deeply integrated into the local landscape.

Uphall
Uphall Golf Club is a premier parkland course located in West Lothian, established in 1895. The course is situated on the banks of the Broxburn, which acts as a natural and often treacherous hazard on several holes. The layout is characterized by its mature woodland and remarkably well-manicured fairways, offering a sense of total seclusion despite its central location. It has a strong competitive history and frequently hosts West Lothian County amateur events.

The club is known for its friendly, professional atmosphere and its commitment to high-quality conditioning. Notable for its "thinking man's" layout, Uphall requires a high degree of accuracy to navigate the narrow, tree-lined corridors and avoid the water hazards. The signature 13th hole, "The Canal" requires a steady nerve on the approach. It is a popular venue for society outings and corporate days, offering a polished and engaging parkland experience that remains a cornerstone of the regional golfing scene.

Vale of Leven
Vale of Leven Golf Club is a spectacular and historic parkland-moorland hybrid perched on the hills overlooking Loch Lomond. Established in 1907, the course offers panoramic views that stretch from the loch to the peaks of the Southern Highlands. The layout is characterized by its significant elevation changes and its exposure to the breezes, which act as a constant defender of par. It is a tactical course where local knowledge is key to navigating the various blind shots.

The club is a focal point of the local community and is known for its unpretentious and welcoming membership. Notable for its fast, true greens and its challenging par-threes, Vale of Leven is a regular host for regional amateur championships. The signature view from the clubhouse over the Leven Valley is one of the most photographed in the region. It is a traditional, well-maintained club that provides a spirited and physically engaging round of golf, capturing the rugged, green spirit of the West Highlands.

West Kilbride
West Kilbride Golf Club is a hallowed links masterpiece located on the Ayrshire coast. Founded in 1893 and significantly redesigned by the legendary James Braid, the course is a traditional "out and back" links that hugs the shoreline of the Firth of Clyde. It offers spectacular, uninterrupted views across to the Isle of Arran and the Ailsa Craig. The layout is characterized by its firm, sandy turf, deep bunkers, and the ever-present sea breeze.

The club has a prestigious tournament history, frequently hosting the Scottish Girls' Championship and serving as a qualifying venue for the Open. Notable for its fast, true greens and its challenging middle stretch through the dunes, West Kilbride is a "pure" links experience of the highest order. It is a refined and welcoming club that maintains a strong sense of its 19th-century heritage. For those seeking an authentic, championship-standard links round with a world-class backdrop, West Kilbride is an essential and rewarding stop.

West Lothian
West Lothian Golf Club is a premier hillside parkland course located near Bo'ness. Established in 1892, the course offers some of the most expansive views in the central belt, stretching across the Firth of Forth to the Ochil Hills and the mountains of the Southern Highlands. The layout is a tactical masterpiece characterized by significant elevation changes and mature woodland.


The club has a prestigious tournament history, frequently hosting the Scottish Mid-Amateur Championship and regional PGA Scotland events. Notable for its impeccably fast, sloping greens and its "thinking man's" routing, it requires a creative approach to avoid the deep bunkers. The signature 14th hole, "The Airngath" offers a dramatic tee shot with a backdrop that is among the most photographed in the region. It is a professional and welcoming club that provides a polished and physically engaging round of golf.

Westerwood
The Westerwood Golf & Spa Resort in Cumbernauld features a modern championship course designed by the legendary Seve Ballesteros and Dave Thomas. Opened in 1989, the layout is a spectacular parkland-moorland hybrid that winds through silver birch and pine forests. It is famous for its "Signature" 15th hole, a par-three played over a deep, heather-filled ravine to a green carved into the hillside.

The course is notorious for its challenging bunkering and its large, undulating greens that reflect Seve's creative flair. Notable for its world-class resort facilities, Westerwood is a favorite for corporate golf days and national amateur qualifiers. It offers a "Tour-standard" experience where the wind off the surrounding hills adds an extra layer of difficulty. It is a polished, high-gloss destination that provides a visually stunning and technically demanding round in the heart of the central belt.

Westgate
Westgate Golf Club (now largely integrated into the broader Edinburgh municipal and community network) was a historic 9-hole nursery for the game in the capital. As a public-access facility, it served as a vital entry point for juniors and beginners for decades. The layout was relatively flat and open, designed to encourage a fast and enjoyable round without the punishing hazards of the championship tracks.

While it lacked the architectural prestige of the Braid or MacKenzie designs, it represented the "social" heart of the sport—unpretentious, affordable, and inclusive. Many of the city's top amateur players began their journey on Westgate's fairways. It stands as a reminder of the importance of accessible urban golf spaces in fostering a lifelong love for the game.

Whalsay
Whalsay Golf Club holds the title of the most northerly 18-hole golf course in the British Isles. Located on the "Bonnie Isle" of Whalsay in Shetland, the course is an elemental experience perched on the edge of the Atlantic. The layout is a rugged moorland links where there are no trees to block the wind; instead, you are surrounded by dramatic sea cliffs, peat bogs, and the constant sound of the ocean.

The club is known for its incredibly warm Shetland welcome and its "Midnight Sun" tournaments. Notable for its isolation and its cinematic views of the northern isles, Whalsay requires a masterclass in low-ball flight and imagination. The turf is remarkably springy and fast-draining despite the harsh climate. For the adventurous golfer, Whalsay offers a raw, beautiful, and unforgettable golfing frontier that marks the literal edge of the sport in the UK.

Whitburn
Whitburn Golf Club is a high-quality parkland-moorland hybrid located in West Lothian, established in 1933. The course is situated on high ground, offering panoramic views across the Forth Valley. It is characterized by its wide fairways and strategic clusters of trees, providing a fair but testing round that rewards both power and precision.

The club is a vibrant hub for the local community and is known for its friendly, forward-thinking atmosphere. While it is a relatively modern course, it has quickly established a reputation for its consistent conditioning and its challenging finishing stretch. Notable for its exposure to the breezes, Whitburn requires a thoughtful approach to club selection. It is a popular venue for society outings, offering a high-value and professional golfing experience in a tranquil countryside setting.

Whitekirk Hill
Whitekirk Hill in East Lothian was once home to a world-class championship course that hosted the European Challenge Tour. While the original 18-hole layout has transitioned into a luxury eco-resort focused on leisure and family activities, the site remains a point of interest for its historic role in the East Lothian "Golf Coast" boom of the 1990s. The land is still beautifully maintained, reflecting the lush, rolling terrain that once challenged the world's rising professionals.

Today, Whitekirk Hill serves as a premier destination for golfers staying in the region to play nearby North Berwick and Muirfield. It represents the evolution of the Scottish golf estate—moving from a pure sporting venue to a comprehensive lifestyle destination—while still honoring its high-quality landscape and its place in the modern history of the "Cradle of Golf."

Whitemoss
Whitemoss Golf Club, located near Perth, is a modern and highly accessible 18-hole parkland course that opened in the 1990s. The layout is relatively flat and winds through young woodland and over rolling farmland. It was designed to provide a relaxed and inclusive environment, making it a favorite for families, juniors, and those looking for a stress-free round.

The club features an excellent driving range and a professional coaching academy. While it lacks the ancient history of its Highland neighbors, Whitemoss offers a polished and high-value experience with impeccably true greens. Notable for its friendly, "pay-and-play" atmosphere, it has become a vital hub for the growth of the game in Perthshire. It represents the modern, welcoming face of the sport, offering a high-standard facility that remains accessible to all.

Wigtown & Bladnoch
Wigtown & Bladnoch Golf Club is a scenic and historic 9-hole parkland course situated on the shores of the Solway Firth. Established in 1905, the course offers panoramic views across the Wigtown Bay nature reserve. The layout is characterized by its lush greenery and its proximity to the Bladnoch Distillery, adding a sensory layer of malt whisky to the sea air.

The club is known for its warm, South West hospitality and its unpretentious atmosphere. While it is a shorter course, the sloping fairways and small greens require a high degree of accuracy. Notable for its peaceful, secluded setting and its commitment to traditional values, it is a favorite for visitors exploring the "Book Town" of Wigtown. It is a quintessential Scottish village club that provides a tranquil and high-value round of golf in a setting of exceptional natural beauty.

Wigtownshire County
Wigtownshire County Golf Club, located at Glenluce, is a premier 18-hole links course situated on the shores of Luce Bay. Established in 1894, the course is a traditional links characterized by its firm turf, sandy dunes, and the constant presence of the sea breeze. It has a prestigious history and has served as a Final Qualifying venue for the Open Championship in the past.

The layout is a classic "out and back" links that rewards creative shot-making and a low ball flight. Notable for its incredibly fast greens and its challenging middle stretch through the gorse, the "County" is widely regarded as one of the best-value links in Scotland. The ruins of Glenluce Abbey provide a dramatic backdrop to several holes. It is a refined and welcoming club that offers a "pure" and historic links experience, making it a centerpiece of the South West golf trail.

Winterfield
Winterfield Golf Club in Dunbar is a spectacular 18-hole links-parkland hybrid that offers some of the most dramatic coastal views in East Lothian. Established in 1935, the course is situated on a headland overlooking the Firth of Forth and the Bass Rock. It is a "natural" course characterized by its significant elevation changes and its exposure to the fierce North Sea gales.

The club is known for its friendly, community-focused atmosphere and its proximity to the historic town center. Notable for its signature 1st hole—a par-three played straight toward the ocean—Winterfield provides a spirited and exhilarating test. While shorter than its championship neighbors, its defense lies in the wind and the tricky, sloping greens. It is an honest, traditional club that offers a wild and visually stunning round of golf, representing the "fun" side of the East Lothian links experience.

Wishaw
Wishaw Golf Club is a historic parkland course in North Lanarkshire with roots dating back to 1894. The current layout was designed in 1935 by the legendary James Braid after the club moved to its present site at Foggielea. It is a quintessential Braid design, making expert use of the natural undulations to create a strategic and fair test of golf. The course is characterized by its mature tree-lined fairways and exceptionally true, undulating greens.


The club has a long-standing reputation for its high-quality conditioning and its welcoming, family-oriented atmosphere. Notable for its "humps and hollows"—a classic Braid feature—it requires a sharp short game to navigate the tricky surrounds. While it sits within a busy part of the central belt, the course feels remarkably secluded and offers lovely views of the surrounding countryside. It is a traditional club that takes great pride in its heritage, offering a polished and engaging parkland round that remains a favorite in the Lanarkshire golfing circuit.


Woll (The Woll)
The Woll Golf Course, located at the New Woll Estate in Ashkirk near Selkirk, is one of the most popular and modern golfing destinations in the Scottish Borders. Originally opened as a 9-hole course in 1993, it was expanded to a full 18-hole championship layout by 2004. It is a beautiful parkland course that follows the contours of the Ale Valley, featuring water hazards on several holes, including a spectacular 17th hole where the green is almost entirely surrounded by water.


The club is famous for its "Play, Stay, and Eat" concept, featuring luxury self-catering cottages and an award-winning restaurant. Notable for being voted into the Top 100 Golf Course Society Venues in the UK, it offers a high-gloss, resort-style experience. The greens are built to USGA specifications, ensuring excellent year-round playability. The Woll is known as "The Friendliest Course in the Borders" providing a high-value, professional, and scenic round of golf that is a mandatory stop for anyone touring the south of Scotland.


Woodlands (Woodlands Glencoe)
Woodlands Golf Course, often referred to as The Dragon's Tooth, is a world-renowned 9-hole masterpiece located at the foot of Glencoe. Situated on the shores of Loch Linnhe, the course is shadowed by the majestic peaks of Sgorr Dhearg and Sgorr Dhonuill. It has been ranked by Golf Magazine as one of the Top 50 9-hole courses in the world and is widely considered the best 9-hole track in Scotland.


The layout features USGA-specification greens and a design that is both visually stunning and technically demanding. Notable for its dramatic elevation changes and the "Dragon's Tooth" mountain backdrop, it offers a "boutique" golfing experience of the highest order. The club operates on a relaxed "turn up and play" basis and features a charming clubhouse with an honesty bar. For any golfer traveling through the Highlands, Woodlands provides a raw, beautiful, and spiritually moving round of golf that captures the very essence of the Scottish landscape.
